Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
The Purpose of the Eighth Edition
Author opens with praise and states his purpose for the edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's aim in producing this new edition and the importance he places on continuous revision and striving for perfection.

Core Idea
Revision and refinement are a scholar's ongoing journey toward perfection.

In this opening passage of the eighth edition, the author sets the stage by expressing his dedication to improving his work through revision, verification, and addition. He sees this not as a correction of errors but as a continuous effort to reach the ideal. Let's read his own words.

Guided Path
1
Read the Basmala and Hamdala
Notice the traditional opening. It establishes the tone of the author's humility and reliance on Allah.
These are standard but significant.
2
Identify the author's stated purpose
The author says this edition is 'another step of revision, verification, and addition.' What does this tell you about his approach to his work?
3
Reflect on the concept of perfection
He says he strives to reach perfection 'to the utmost.' Why is this important in Islamic scholarship?
Perfection is sought but never fully attained; it drives continuous improvement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة الطبعة الثامنة
الحمد لله حمداً يوافي نعمه ويكافئ مزيده . ياربنا لك الحمد كما ينبغي لجلال وجهك ولعظيم سلطانك . والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد المبعوث رحمة للعالمين ، وعلى آله وصحبه صلاة وسلاماً دائمين إلى يوم الدين
وبعد فهذه خطوة أخرى من خطوات التنقيح والتحقيق والزيادة ، التي وفقني الله للقيام بها بصدد خدمة هذا الكتاب إخراجاً وتنقيحاً وسعياً به ـ جهد المستطاع - إلى الكمال
عز
لقد أضفت عليه في إحدى الطبعات السابقة، في بحث الدليل على وجود الله وجل ، عرضاً موجزاً للأدلة على تهافت الفلسفة المادية ، وجنوحها عن قوانين العلم وأصول المنطق ، في كل من أصولها المادية ، وفروعها التاريخية ، وكان ذلك قبل أن يتفضل علي المولى عز وجل بالتوفيق لإخراج كتابي : « نقض أوهام المادية الجدلية » الذي أفردته في هذا الموضوع
تكشف
ثم أضفت عليه ، في طبعة لاحقة ، بحثاً مفصلاً يتضمن عرض أهم النظريات الحديثة التي تفرض تطور الإنسان من أنواع حيوانية أقل شأناً ، ثم مناقشتها بالأدلة العلمية التي [عن] اضطرابها وبطلانها، وعن كونها ليست أكثر من فرضيات مبتورة عن أي دليل علمي يكسبها أي رسوخ في تربة العلم أو حتى البحث العلمي . ولقد طبع هذا الكتاب ، بعد ذلك ، مرات على الأوفست ، دون أي زيادة أو تعديل ، لا لشيء سوى ضيق وقتي عن إمكان الرجوع إلى بحوثه بتحقيق جديد ، عما قد يكون فيه من ثغرات تحتاج إلى إضافات وبحوث لاحقة .
والتنقيب
أما الآن فقد هيا الله تعالى لي ، بفضله وكرمه ، بحبوحة من الوقت ، يسرت لي استعراض بحوث هذا الكتاب من جديد ، ابتغاء القيام بمزيد من العناية المجددة ببحوثه التي لا جرم أنها أخطر ما يمكن أن يصرف إليه الإنسان عقله من مسائل الكون وعلومه فبذلت كل ما أملك من جهد في سبيل ألا أمرّ على عبارة تحتاج إلى مزيد من الإيضاح الذي يناله طوقي ، إلا بعد أن أستبدل بها عبارة أتم دلالة ووضوحاً ، وأن أفتش عن أي كلمة قد توهم ( في نطاق التعبير الدقيق عن شيء من صفات الله تعالى أو أفعاله ( معنى لا يتفق مع كماله المطلق عز وجل ، وسموه عن كل مثال ونظير، فأستبدل بها ما يكون أدق دلالة على المعنى المطلوب ، وأبعد عن المعاني المألوفة للمخلوقين.
·
ولا ريب أن ساحة التعبير ، تدق أمام الإنسان ، عندما يريد أن يتحدث عن الله وصفاته وأفعاله ، ويخوض في دقائق المسائل الإلهية .. إذ إن كثيراً من الألفاظ لا تصلح للتعبير بها في هذا المقام ، بسبب أنها مصوغة للدلالة على حدود وأبعاد وتحيزات هي في جملتها من عوارض المخلوقين
ثم إني بذلت جهداً آخر ، في سبيل إضافات وتفصيلات دعت إليها ضرورة التوضيح وإزالة اللبس ، وقد جاء بعضها في صلب الكتاب ، وأثبت بعضها الآخر تعليقاً في أماكنها المناسبة
·
ومن أهم هذه الإضافات الضرورية ، مبحث الردّة وأسبابها . فقد شعرت بأن ضرورة قصوى تدعو إلى تدارك هذا البحث وإثباته ، مفصلاً ، في صلب هذا الكتاب
ولئن كنت قد قصرت في الاهتمام به في الطبعات السابقة ، فذلك لأن صفة التقصير شأني ، ولأن هذه الضرورة لم تكن ماثلة في المجتمع من قبل .. فمن جديد أخذت تطوف بأفكار بعض الناشئة تصورات باطلة لا أصل لها عن الردّة وأسبابها ، لعل مبعثها ردود فعل هيجتها العاطفة ، وأعوزتها ضوابط العلم والمعرفة
ومن أهم الأسباب التي تدعو الباحث إلى التوسع في [يا كتب] ، الأوضاع الفكرية والاجتماعية الطارئة التي تفرض نفسها على المجتمع لأسباب مختلفة .
وعلى كل حال ، فقد بذلت جهداً جديداً في خدمة هذا الكتاب ، رجوت أن يقفز به قفزة أخرى نحو الكمال المنشود . راجيا الله عز وجل أن يقيني من كل ما قد يحبط عملي
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction to the Eighth Edition. Praise be to Allah, praise that matches His blessings and suffices for His increase. Our Lord, to You be praise as is befitting the majesty of Your face and the greatness of Your authority. And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family and companions, prayers and peace everlasting until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: this is another step of revision, verification, and addition, which Allah has enabled me to undertake in serving this book in terms of publication, revision, and striving to the utmost to reach perfection. Mighty. I added to it in one of the previous editions, in the discussion of the proof for the existence of Allah the Exalted, a brief presentation of the proofs for the incoherence of materialist philosophy and its deviation from the laws of science and the principles of logic, both in its materialist foundations and its historical branches. That was before my Lord the Exalted bestowed upon me the success to produce my book 'Refutation of the Illusions of Dialectical Materialism,' which I devoted to this topic. [unclear] Then I added to it, in a later edition, a detailed discussion covering the most important modern theories that posit the evolution of humans from lower animal types, then discussing them with scientific proofs that [about?] their confusion and falsehood, and that they are nothing more than hypotheses severed from any scientific evidence that would give them any firmness in the soil of science or even scientific research. After that, this book was reprinted several times by offset, without any addition or modification, only due to my lack of time to review its discussions with new research, regarding any gaps that might need subsequent additions and investigations. And now Allah the Exalted has granted me, by His grace and generosity, ample time, enabling me to review the discussions of this book anew, seeking to provide renewed care for its discussions, which are undoubtedly the most serious matters that a person can devote his mind to—the issues of the universe and its sciences. So I exerted all the effort I could to ensure that I would not pass over a statement that needs further clarification within my capacity without replacing it with a more complete and clear expression, and to search for any word that might imply (within the scope of precise expression about something of Allah's attributes or actions) a meaning inconsistent with His absolute perfection, Exalted and Majestic, and His transcendence above any likeness or counterpart, and replace it with what is more precise in indicating the intended meaning and further from the usual meanings of created beings. And there is no doubt that the field of expression becomes narrow for a person when he wants to speak about Allah, His attributes, and His actions, and delves into the subtleties of divine matters. For many words are unsuitable for expression in this context because they are coined to indicate limits, dimensions, and biases which in their entirety are accidents of created beings. Then I exerted another effort for additions and details necessitated by the need for clarification and removal of confusion. Some of them came in the body of the book, and others I inserted as notes in their appropriate places. Among the most important of these necessary additions is the section on apostasy and its causes. I felt that an urgent necessity calls for addressing this discussion and recording it, in detail, in the body of this book. Even if I had fallen short in paying attention to it in previous editions, that is because deficiency is my habit, and because this necessity was not present in society before. Recently, false misconceptions with no basis about apostasy and its causes began to circulate among the thoughts of some youth, perhaps triggered by emotional reactions lacking the controls of knowledge and science. Among the most important reasons that call a researcher to expand on [something?] are the emergent intellectual and social conditions that impose themselves on society for various reasons. In any case, I made a new effort in serving this book, hoping that it would leap another leap towards the desired perfection. Hoping from Allah the Exalted to protect me from everything that might nullify my work.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the eighth edition of his book. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then proceeds to explain the purpose of this edition: to carry out further revision, verification, and addition. The author mentions that in a previous edition he added a critique of materialist philosophy, including a summary of arguments against it, which later led to a separate book on dialectical materialism. He also added a detailed refutation of evolutionary theories that claim human descent from lower animals, arguing that they are baseless hypotheses without scientific evidence. After several reprints without changes due to time constraints, he now has the opportunity to review the entire book anew. He emphasizes his careful attention to language, especially when speaking about Allah's attributes and actions, because many ordinary words imply limitations or imperfections that are only appropriate for created beings. He replaced any phrase that might suggest a meaning inconsistent with Allah's absolute perfection. Finally, he discusses the most significant new addition: a detailed section on apostasy and its causes. He explains that this became necessary because false ideas about apostasy have recently spread among younger generations, stemming from emotional reactions rather than sound knowledge. The author concludes by expressing his hope that this effort will bring the book closer to perfection and asks Allah to protect his work from being nullified.

Key Terms
تنقيح
تحقيق
زيادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a new edition means the previous one was wrong or deficient.
Correction: The author clarifies that revision is a continuous process of improvement, not a correction of fundamental errors. He speaks of 'another step' toward perfection, implying it's a cumulative effort.

Checkpoint
What three actions does the author mention as his purpose for this edition?
A) Revision, verification, and addition
B) Correction, expansion, and commentary
C) Translation, summarization, and annotation
D) Publication, distribution, and marketing

Key Takeaway
The author views each edition as an opportunity to refine his work, striving for perfection through revision, verification, and addition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you revised a strongly held belief about your deen? What discomfort did that process bring, and did you embrace it as a 'step toward perfection' or resist it out of pride?
?
The author humbly admits he is still striving for perfection. Are you willing to admit that your current understanding of Islam might need 'revision, verification, or addition'? What is holding you back?
?
If your personal 'eighth edition' of faith came out today, what would need to change? Will you take one concrete step this week to revise an area you had previously considered final?

Method of Learning
intermediate
5 min
Previous Additions: Refuting Materialism and Evolution
Author details his earlier additions to the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key previous additions the author made to his book: a critique of materialist philosophy and a scientific refutation of evolutionary theories.

Core Idea
The author tackles two major modern challenges: materialism and evolution.

After stating his general purpose, the author recalls two significant additions from earlier editions: a critique of materialist philosophy and a detailed refutation of evolutionary theories that claim human descent from lower animals. He summarizes his approach and notes that these were precursors to his separate book on dialectical materialism.

Guided Path
1
Read about the first addition
The author added a brief critique of materialist philosophy, covering both its foundations and historical branches. Note that he later expanded this into a separate book.
This shows his systematic approach.
2
Read about the second addition
He added a detailed discussion of modern theories of human evolution, arguing they are baseless hypotheses lacking scientific evidence.
He emphasizes the scientific critique.
3
Note the reason for no further changes
After these additions, the book was reprinted without changes due to lack of time for further research.
This sets up for the current edition's thorough revision.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction to the Eighth Edition. Praise be to Allah, praise that matches His blessings and suffices for His increase. Our Lord, to You be praise as is befitting the majesty of Your face and the greatness of Your authority. And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family and companions, prayers and peace everlasting until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: this is another step of revision, verification, and addition, which Allah has enabled me to undertake in serving this book in terms of publication, revision, and striving to the utmost to reach perfection. Mighty. I added to it in one of the previous editions, in the discussion of the proof for the existence of Allah the Exalted, a brief presentation of the proofs for the incoherence of materialist philosophy and its deviation from the laws of science and the principles of logic, both in its materialist foundations and its historical branches. That was before my Lord the Exalted bestowed upon me the success to produce my book 'Refutation of the Illusions of Dialectical Materialism,' which I devoted to this topic. [unclear] Then I added to it, in a later edition, a detailed discussion covering the most important modern theories that posit the evolution of humans from lower animal types, then discussing them with scientific proofs that [about?] their confusion and falsehood, and that they are nothing more than hypotheses severed from any scientific evidence that would give them any firmness in the soil of science or even scientific research. After that, this book was reprinted several times by offset, without any addition or modification, only due to my lack of time to review its discussions with new research, regarding any gaps that might need subsequent additions and investigations. And now Allah the Exalted has granted me, by His grace and generosity, ample time, enabling me to review the discussions of this book anew, seeking to provide renewed care for its discussions, which are undoubtedly the most serious matters that a person can devote his mind to—the issues of the universe and its sciences. So I exerted all the effort I could to ensure that I would not pass over a statement that needs further clarification within my capacity without replacing it with a more complete and clear expression, and to search for any word that might imply (within the scope of precise expression about something of Allah's attributes or actions) a meaning inconsistent with His absolute perfection, Exalted and Majestic, and His transcendence above any likeness or counterpart, and replace it with what is more precise in indicating the intended meaning and further from the usual meanings of created beings. And there is no doubt that the field of expression becomes narrow for a person when he wants to speak about Allah, His attributes, and His actions, and delves into the subtleties of divine matters. For many words are unsuitable for expression in this context because they are coined to indicate limits, dimensions, and biases which in their entirety are accidents of created beings. Then I exerted another effort for additions and details necessitated by the need for clarification and removal of confusion. Some of them came in the body of the book, and others I inserted as notes in their appropriate places. Among the most important of these necessary additions is the section on apostasy and its causes. I felt that an urgent necessity calls for addressing this discussion and recording it, in detail, in the body of this book. Even if I had fallen short in paying attention to it in previous editions, that is because deficiency is my habit, and because this necessity was not present in society before. Recently, false misconceptions with no basis about apostasy and its causes began to circulate among the thoughts of some youth, perhaps triggered by emotional reactions lacking the controls of knowledge and science. Among the most important reasons that call a researcher to expand on [something?] are the emergent intellectual and social conditions that impose themselves on society for various reasons. In any case, I made a new effort in serving this book, hoping that it would leap another leap towards the desired perfection. Hoping from Allah the Exalted to protect me from everything that might nullify my work.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the eighth edition of his book. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then proceeds to explain the purpose of this edition: to carry out further revision, verification, and addition. The author mentions that in a previous edition he added a critique of materialist philosophy, including a summary of arguments against it, which later led to a separate book on dialectical materialism. He also added a detailed refutation of evolutionary theories that claim human descent from lower animals, arguing that they are baseless hypotheses without scientific evidence. After several reprints without changes due to time constraints, he now has the opportunity to review the entire book anew. He emphasizes his careful attention to language, especially when speaking about Allah's attributes and actions, because many ordinary words imply limitations or imperfections that are only appropriate for created beings. He replaced any phrase that might suggest a meaning inconsistent with Allah's absolute perfection. Finally, he discusses the most significant new addition: a detailed section on apostasy and its causes. He explains that this became necessary because false ideas about apostasy have recently spread among younger generations, stemming from emotional reactions rather than sound knowledge. The author concludes by expressing his hope that this effort will bring the book closer to perfection and asks Allah to protect his work from being nullified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author's critique of evolution is purely philosophical.
Correction: The author explicitly states he used scientific evidence (الأدلة العلمية) to refute these theories, showing their inconsistency and lack of evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what did he add in a later edition after the materialist critique?
A) A chapter on divine attributes
B) A discussion on apostasy
C) A detailed refutation of evolutionary theories
D) A new introduction

Key Takeaway
The author previously incorporated critiques of materialism and evolution, using scientific arguments to challenge modern ideologies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author dedicated years to meticulously refuting ideologies that challenge faith. Have you ever critically examined a widely accepted idea (like materialism or evolution) with the same rigor? If not, what is holding you back from seeking the truth yourself?
?
The author did not simply repeat others' arguments but produced original scholarly work. In what area of your own life are you content to follow the majority without personal investigation, and what step can you take this week to change that?
?
This lesson shows the author's commitment to addressing intellectual challenges to Islam. When you encounter a doubt about your faith, do you actively seek out well-reasoned responses, or do you avoid the question? What would it cost you to engage honestly with that doubt today?

6 min
Precision in Speaking About Allah's Attributes
Author explains his careful revision of language about Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the author's meticulous effort to choose words that accurately convey Allah's attributes without implying any imperfection or similarity to creation.

Core Idea
Every word about Allah must be purified from human limitations.

The author then explains the rigorous process he undertook to revise every expression in the book, especially those related to Allah's attributes and actions. He replaced any phrase that might suggest imperfection or anthropomorphism. This lesson highlights the extraordinary care required when speaking about the Divine.

Guided Path
1
Understand the author's criterion
The author says he replaced any statement that needed clarification with a clearer one, and scrutinized words that might imply meanings inconsistent with Allah's perfection.
This shows his commitment to theological precision.
2
Identify the challenge
He notes that human language is inherently inadequate for discussing Allah because words are shaped by created concepts of limits and dimensions.
This is a key insight in Islamic theology.
3
Notice the dual effort
He made efforts both to replace expressions and to add clarifying details, either in the main text or as footnotes.
His method is thorough and systematic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة الطبعة الثامنة
الحمد لله حمداً يوافي نعمه ويكافئ مزيده . ياربنا لك الحمد كما ينبغي لجلال وجهك ولعظيم سلطانك . والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد المبعوث رحمة للعالمين ، وعلى آله وصحبه صلاة وسلاماً دائمين إلى يوم الدين
وبعد فهذه خطوة أخرى من خطوات التنقيح والتحقيق والزيادة ، التي وفقني الله للقيام بها بصدد خدمة هذا الكتاب إخراجاً وتنقيحاً وسعياً به ـ جهد المستطاع - إلى الكمال
عز
لقد أضفت عليه في إحدى الطبعات السابقة، في بحث الدليل على وجود الله وجل ، عرضاً موجزاً للأدلة على تهافت الفلسفة المادية ، وجنوحها عن قوانين العلم وأصول المنطق ، في كل من أصولها المادية ، وفروعها التاريخية ، وكان ذلك قبل أن يتفضل علي المولى عز وجل بالتوفيق لإخراج كتابي : « نقض أوهام المادية الجدلية » الذي أفردته في هذا الموضوع
تكشف
ثم أضفت عليه ، في طبعة لاحقة ، بحثاً مفصلاً يتضمن عرض أهم النظريات الحديثة التي تفرض تطور الإنسان من أنواع حيوانية أقل شأناً ، ثم مناقشتها بالأدلة العلمية التي [عن] اضطرابها وبطلانها، وعن كونها ليست أكثر من فرضيات مبتورة عن أي دليل علمي يكسبها أي رسوخ في تربة العلم أو حتى البحث العلمي . ولقد طبع هذا الكتاب ، بعد ذلك ، مرات على الأوفست ، دون أي زيادة أو تعديل ، لا لشيء سوى ضيق وقتي عن إمكان الرجوع إلى بحوثه بتحقيق جديد ، عما قد يكون فيه من ثغرات تحتاج إلى إضافات وبحوث لاحقة .
والتنقيب
أما الآن فقد هيا الله تعالى لي ، بفضله وكرمه ، بحبوحة من الوقت ، يسرت لي استعراض بحوث هذا الكتاب من جديد ، ابتغاء القيام بمزيد من العناية المجددة ببحوثه التي لا جرم أنها أخطر ما يمكن أن يصرف إليه الإنسان عقله من مسائل الكون وعلومه فبذلت كل ما أملك من جهد في سبيل ألا أمرّ على عبارة تحتاج إلى مزيد من الإيضاح الذي يناله طوقي ، إلا بعد أن أستبدل بها عبارة أتم دلالة ووضوحاً ، وأن أفتش عن أي كلمة قد توهم ( في نطاق التعبير الدقيق عن شيء من صفات الله تعالى أو أفعاله ( معنى لا يتفق مع كماله المطلق عز وجل ، وسموه عن كل مثال ونظير، فأستبدل بها ما يكون أدق دلالة على المعنى المطلوب ، وأبعد عن المعاني المألوفة للمخلوقين.
·
ولا ريب أن ساحة التعبير ، تدق أمام الإنسان ، عندما يريد أن يتحدث عن الله وصفاته وأفعاله ، ويخوض في دقائق المسائل الإلهية .. إذ إن كثيراً من الألفاظ لا تصلح للتعبير بها في هذا المقام ، بسبب أنها مصوغة للدلالة على حدود وأبعاد وتحيزات هي في جملتها من عوارض المخلوقين
ثم إني بذلت جهداً آخر ، في سبيل إضافات وتفصيلات دعت إليها ضرورة التوضيح وإزالة اللبس ، وقد جاء بعضها في صلب الكتاب ، وأثبت بعضها الآخر تعليقاً في أماكنها المناسبة
·
ومن أهم هذه الإضافات الضرورية ، مبحث الردّة وأسبابها . فقد شعرت بأن ضرورة قصوى تدعو إلى تدارك هذا البحث وإثباته ، مفصلاً ، في صلب هذا الكتاب
ولئن كنت قد قصرت في الاهتمام به في الطبعات السابقة ، فذلك لأن صفة التقصير شأني ، ولأن هذه الضرورة لم تكن ماثلة في المجتمع من قبل .. فمن جديد أخذت تطوف بأفكار بعض الناشئة تصورات باطلة لا أصل لها عن الردّة وأسبابها ، لعل مبعثها ردود فعل هيجتها العاطفة ، وأعوزتها ضوابط العلم والمعرفة
ومن أهم الأسباب التي تدعو الباحث إلى التوسع في [يا كتب] ، الأوضاع الفكرية والاجتماعية الطارئة التي تفرض نفسها على المجتمع لأسباب مختلفة .
وعلى كل حال ، فقد بذلت جهداً جديداً في خدمة هذا الكتاب ، رجوت أن يقفز به قفزة أخرى نحو الكمال المنشود . راجيا الله عز وجل أن يقيني من كل ما قد يحبط عملي
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction to the Eighth Edition. Praise be to Allah, praise that matches His blessings and suffices for His increase. Our Lord, to You be praise as is befitting the majesty of Your face and the greatness of Your authority. And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family and companions, prayers and peace everlasting until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: this is another step of revision, verification, and addition, which Allah has enabled me to undertake in serving this book in terms of publication, revision, and striving to the utmost to reach perfection. Mighty. I added to it in one of the previous editions, in the discussion of the proof for the existence of Allah the Exalted, a brief presentation of the proofs for the incoherence of materialist philosophy and its deviation from the laws of science and the principles of logic, both in its materialist foundations and its historical branches. That was before my Lord the Exalted bestowed upon me the success to produce my book 'Refutation of the Illusions of Dialectical Materialism,' which I devoted to this topic. [unclear] Then I added to it, in a later edition, a detailed discussion covering the most important modern theories that posit the evolution of humans from lower animal types, then discussing them with scientific proofs that [about?] their confusion and falsehood, and that they are nothing more than hypotheses severed from any scientific evidence that would give them any firmness in the soil of science or even scientific research. After that, this book was reprinted several times by offset, without any addition or modification, only due to my lack of time to review its discussions with new research, regarding any gaps that might need subsequent additions and investigations. And now Allah the Exalted has granted me, by His grace and generosity, ample time, enabling me to review the discussions of this book anew, seeking to provide renewed care for its discussions, which are undoubtedly the most serious matters that a person can devote his mind to—the issues of the universe and its sciences. So I exerted all the effort I could to ensure that I would not pass over a statement that needs further clarification within my capacity without replacing it with a more complete and clear expression, and to search for any word that might imply (within the scope of precise expression about something of Allah's attributes or actions) a meaning inconsistent with His absolute perfection, Exalted and Majestic, and His transcendence above any likeness or counterpart, and replace it with what is more precise in indicating the intended meaning and further from the usual meanings of created beings. And there is no doubt that the field of expression becomes narrow for a person when he wants to speak about Allah, His attributes, and His actions, and delves into the subtleties of divine matters. For many words are unsuitable for expression in this context because they are coined to indicate limits, dimensions, and biases which in their entirety are accidents of created beings. Then I exerted another effort for additions and details necessitated by the need for clarification and removal of confusion. Some of them came in the body of the book, and others I inserted as notes in their appropriate places. Among the most important of these necessary additions is the section on apostasy and its causes. I felt that an urgent necessity calls for addressing this discussion and recording it, in detail, in the body of this book. Even if I had fallen short in paying attention to it in previous editions, that is because deficiency is my habit, and because this necessity was not present in society before. Recently, false misconceptions with no basis about apostasy and its causes began to circulate among the thoughts of some youth, perhaps triggered by emotional reactions lacking the controls of knowledge and science. Among the most important reasons that call a researcher to expand on [something?] are the emergent intellectual and social conditions that impose themselves on society for various reasons. In any case, I made a new effort in serving this book, hoping that it would leap another leap towards the desired perfection. Hoping from Allah the Exalted to protect me from everything that might nullify my work.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the eighth edition of his book. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then proceeds to explain the purpose of this edition: to carry out further revision, verification, and addition. The author mentions that in a previous edition he added a critique of materialist philosophy, including a summary of arguments against it, which later led to a separate book on dialectical materialism. He also added a detailed refutation of evolutionary theories that claim human descent from lower animals, arguing that they are baseless hypotheses without scientific evidence. After several reprints without changes due to time constraints, he now has the opportunity to review the entire book anew. He emphasizes his careful attention to language, especially when speaking about Allah's attributes and actions, because many ordinary words imply limitations or imperfections that are only appropriate for created beings. He replaced any phrase that might suggest a meaning inconsistent with Allah's absolute perfection. Finally, he discusses the most significant new addition: a detailed section on apostasy and its causes. He explains that this became necessary because false ideas about apostasy have recently spread among younger generations, stemming from emotional reactions rather than sound knowledge. The author concludes by expressing his hope that this effort will bring the book closer to perfection and asks Allah to protect his work from being nullified.

Key Terms
صفات الله
كماله المطلق
التعبير الدقيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author's revisions suggest the previous editions contained theological errors.
Correction: The author does not claim errors; he says he sought to enhance precision and remove any ambiguous phrasing that could be misinterpreted, not that earlier versions were doctrinally wrong.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say many words are unsuitable for speaking about Allah?
A) Because they are too complex
B) Because they are coined for created beings and imply limits
C) Because they are not in Arabic
D) Because they are too modern

Key Takeaway
The author rigorously revised expressions about Allah to ensure they reflect His absolute perfection and transcendence, using precise language and clarifying additions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray or make dua, do you ever use words that unconsciously describe Allah in human terms? After this lesson, what specific phrase will you avoid and what will you replace it with?
?
The author devoted immense effort to purify every expression about Allah. How much time have you spent examining your own speech about Him? Will you commit to reviewing and revising at least one common phrase you use by the end of this week?
?
If you truly believe that Allah is absolutely perfect, why do you still use language that borrows from creation when describing Him? What is one step you will take today to speak about Him with greater reverence and precision?

5 min
The New Addition on Apostasy and Its Causes
Author introduces his new section on apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's rationale for adding a detailed section on apostasy (الردّة) and its causes, and the societal context that prompted it.

Core Idea
Intellectual challenges require new theological discussions.

In the final part of his introduction, the author identifies the most significant new addition: a detailed discussion on apostasy and its causes. He explains that false ideas about apostasy have recently spread among youth due to emotional reactions lacking sound knowledge. This addition is a response to emergent intellectual and social conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the new addition
The author says the most important new addition is the section on apostasy and its causes. He felt an urgent need to address it.
2
Understand the context
He explains that false concepts about apostasy have spread among some youth, driven by emotion rather than knowledge.
This indicates a pressing contemporary issue.
3
Reflect on the broader principle
He notes that intellectual and social conditions can necessitate new discussions in a book.
This shows how scholarship responds to changing circumstances.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction to the Eighth Edition. Praise be to Allah, praise that matches His blessings and suffices for His increase. Our Lord, to You be praise as is befitting the majesty of Your face and the greatness of Your authority. And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family and companions, prayers and peace everlasting until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: this is another step of revision, verification, and addition, which Allah has enabled me to undertake in serving this book in terms of publication, revision, and striving to the utmost to reach perfection. Mighty. I added to it in one of the previous editions, in the discussion of the proof for the existence of Allah the Exalted, a brief presentation of the proofs for the incoherence of materialist philosophy and its deviation from the laws of science and the principles of logic, both in its materialist foundations and its historical branches. That was before my Lord the Exalted bestowed upon me the success to produce my book 'Refutation of the Illusions of Dialectical Materialism,' which I devoted to this topic. [unclear] Then I added to it, in a later edition, a detailed discussion covering the most important modern theories that posit the evolution of humans from lower animal types, then discussing them with scientific proofs that [about?] their confusion and falsehood, and that they are nothing more than hypotheses severed from any scientific evidence that would give them any firmness in the soil of science or even scientific research. After that, this book was reprinted several times by offset, without any addition or modification, only due to my lack of time to review its discussions with new research, regarding any gaps that might need subsequent additions and investigations. And now Allah the Exalted has granted me, by His grace and generosity, ample time, enabling me to review the discussions of this book anew, seeking to provide renewed care for its discussions, which are undoubtedly the most serious matters that a person can devote his mind to—the issues of the universe and its sciences. So I exerted all the effort I could to ensure that I would not pass over a statement that needs further clarification within my capacity without replacing it with a more complete and clear expression, and to search for any word that might imply (within the scope of precise expression about something of Allah's attributes or actions) a meaning inconsistent with His absolute perfection, Exalted and Majestic, and His transcendence above any likeness or counterpart, and replace it with what is more precise in indicating the intended meaning and further from the usual meanings of created beings. And there is no doubt that the field of expression becomes narrow for a person when he wants to speak about Allah, His attributes, and His actions, and delves into the subtleties of divine matters. For many words are unsuitable for expression in this context because they are coined to indicate limits, dimensions, and biases which in their entirety are accidents of created beings. Then I exerted another effort for additions and details necessitated by the need for clarification and removal of confusion. Some of them came in the body of the book, and others I inserted as notes in their appropriate places. Among the most important of these necessary additions is the section on apostasy and its causes. I felt that an urgent necessity calls for addressing this discussion and recording it, in detail, in the body of this book. Even if I had fallen short in paying attention to it in previous editions, that is because deficiency is my habit, and because this necessity was not present in society before. Recently, false misconceptions with no basis about apostasy and its causes began to circulate among the thoughts of some youth, perhaps triggered by emotional reactions lacking the controls of knowledge and science. Among the most important reasons that call a researcher to expand on [something?] are the emergent intellectual and social conditions that impose themselves on society for various reasons. In any case, I made a new effort in serving this book, hoping that it would leap another leap towards the desired perfection. Hoping from Allah the Exalted to protect me from everything that might nullify my work.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the eighth edition of his book. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then proceeds to explain the purpose of this edition: to carry out further revision, verification, and addition. The author mentions that in a previous edition he added a critique of materialist philosophy, including a summary of arguments against it, which later led to a separate book on dialectical materialism. He also added a detailed refutation of evolutionary theories that claim human descent from lower animals, arguing that they are baseless hypotheses without scientific evidence. After several reprints without changes due to time constraints, he now has the opportunity to review the entire book anew. He emphasizes his careful attention to language, especially when speaking about Allah's attributes and actions, because many ordinary words imply limitations or imperfections that are only appropriate for created beings. He replaced any phrase that might suggest a meaning inconsistent with Allah's absolute perfection. Finally, he discusses the most significant new addition: a detailed section on apostasy and its causes. He explains that this became necessary because false ideas about apostasy have recently spread among younger generations, stemming from emotional reactions rather than sound knowledge. The author concludes by expressing his hope that this effort will bring the book closer to perfection and asks Allah to protect his work from being nullified.

The Author's Method: Universal Accessible Proofs
Author explains his approach of presenting evident proofs without artificial barriers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's methodological approach of presenting proofs of God's existence and human accountability as inherently clear and accessible to all rational minds, and the role of artificial coverings in obscuring them.

Core Idea
Divine proofs are clear; only our biases make them seem distant.

This passage opens the book by explaining the author's method. He wrote to present proofs that are not hidden or complicated, but evident and near. The author insists that the only barriers are artificial—created by our own motives and biases. Before diving into the proofs themselves, he wants us to understand that the truth is already within reach.

Guided Path
1
Understand the author's claim
Read the passage and notice that he says there is no real barrier between reason and proofs. The obstacles are artificial coverings.
The Arabic uses 'الغشاوات المصطنعة' – artificial coverings – to emphasize their fabricated nature.
2
Identify the two types of proofs
He mentions proofs of God's existence ('دلائل وجوده الواجب الأزلي') and proofs of human servitude ('دلائل عبودية الإنسان'). Both are equally clear and near.
3
Reflect on universal accessibility
The author emphasizes that his proofs are not limited to any era or civilization; they are current among all minds in all places and ages.
This is a key methodological point: the proof is common, not esoteric.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتبت منذ عامين تقريباً ما ألهمنيه الله من دلائل وجوده الواجب الأزلي ، ودلائل عبودية الإنسان له وارتباطه بمسؤولية خطيرة عظمى تجاهه
وأوضحت أن ليس بين العقل وشيء من هذه الدلائل ، حاجز يحتاج إلى تكلف في اختراقه ، أو مسافة طويلة تحتاج إلى جهد في قطعها . ولكن الغشاوات المصطنعة بدوافع الأغراض والأهواء والأحقاد ، هي التي أوهمت وجود حاجز .. وهي التي خيلت لبعضهم بعد الشقة .. فاحتاج الأمر لقيام من ينبه إلى أن الحاجز وهمي . والشقة بعد خيالي ، وأن الحق ماثل للعيان قريب من الأفهام .
فكان عملي فيما كتبت ، التنبية إلى أدلة ماثلة واضحة قريبة ، لا ابتداع براهين مجهولة بعيدة . وكان سعي كله منصرفاً إلى التعامل مع تلك البراهين العلمية الرائجة لدى جميع العقول وفي سائر الأمكنة والعصور لا مع نوع معين منها قد لا يفقهها إلا صنف معين من الناس أو لم يتعامل بها إلا أصحاب حضارة متميزة في حقبة تاريخية ضيقة
I wrote about two years ago what God inspired me of proofs of His necessary eternal existence, and proofs of man's servitude to Him and his connection to a grave and great responsibility towards Him. And I explained that between reason and any of these proofs there is no barrier requiring effort to penetrate, nor a long distance requiring effort to cross. But the artificial coverings motivated by purposes, whims, and grudges are what gave the illusion of a barrier... and what made some imagine a far distance... So it required someone to alert that the barrier is illusory, and the distance imaginary, and that truth is manifest to the eye and near to understandings. So my work in what I wrote was alerting to evident, clear, near proofs, not inventing unknown, distant proofs. And all my effort was directed to dealing with those scientific proofs current among all minds and in all places and ages, not with a specific type that only a certain class of people might understand or that only the people of a distinguished civilization in a narrow historical period dealt with.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage defines the author's method and the core thesis of his book. He states that he wrote about proofs of God's eternal existence and human accountability. He argues that there is no real barrier between reason and these proofs—the obstacles are artificial, created by selfish motives and biases. The author's task is not to invent novel arguments but to draw attention to proofs that are already evident, clear, and accessible to all people across times and places, not limited to any one civilization or era.

Correction: The author insists that the proofs are clear and near to all understandings; only artificial coverings from biases make them appear distant.

?

?
The author's method is to alert to what is already evident. Where in your life are you seeking complex answers when the truth is already before you? Commit to stopping one intellectual distraction and focusing on a clear proof you have overlooked.

Impact on Believers and Honest Skeptics
Author recounts the book's impact on two groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the book served two distinct audiences: strengthening believers in their faith and providing conclusive proofs that led sincere skeptics to the tranquility of faith.

Core Idea
Conclusive proofs can turn honest seekers into believers.

The author, with gratitude to God, reflects on the reception of his work. He describes two groups that benefited: believers who found their faith deepened, and open-minded skeptics—including former atheists and materialists—who discovered in its pages the conclusive evidence they had been searching for. This lesson explores that dual impact.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author structures the effects on two groups separately.
The opening expresses gratitude; the middle distinguishes believers and 'those with free hearts'.
2
Identify the two groups
Look for the two categories: 'المؤمنون' (believers) and 'أصحاب القلوب الحرة' (those with free hearts). Understand how each group responded.
3
Analyze the transformation of skeptics
The author describes skeptics as arriving at 'طمأنينة الإيمان' (tranquility of faith) through 'براهين علمية قاطعة' (conclusive scientific proofs). Consider why this is significant.
This shows the book's method: rational proofs over emotional appeals.
4
Reflect on the author's purpose
Ask why the author includes this description. It demonstrates the effectiveness of his approach and serves as evidence for his methodology.

ولقد أراد الله جل جلاله - وله الحمد الذي يعجز لساني عن أداء حقه - أن يؤتي هذا العمل ثماره . فأقبلت إليه الناشئة من كل وجهة وصنف ، وتأمله كثير من المثقفين والباحثين على اختلاف وجهاتهم ومشاربهم ..

And God—glorified and exalted be He—and to Him is praise which my tongue is incapable of rendering—willed that this work bear fruit. So the youth turned to it from every direction and class, and many intellectuals and researchers contemplated it despite their different viewpoints and inclinations.
As for the believers, it increased them in faith and they continued with it their persistent effort in calling to the truth.
As for those with free hearts—those whose hearts were not yet inhabited by faith, but whose minds were also not enslaved by whims or desires or overwhelmed in their discernment—many of them found in it their lost object. They said they had long been searching for it, and they concluded their turbulent intellectual journey amidst confused currents of theories and illusions, arriving at the tranquility of faith in God Almighty and guidance to the reality of themselves, sheltering in the shade of conclusive scientific proofs, not relying on incense of emotions and comforting fantasies. And among these were callers to dialectical materialist creeds and saturated with various atheistic theories.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage describes the reception of the book. The author thanks God that the work bore fruit, attracting youth and intellectuals. For believers, it strengthened their faith and commitment to da'wah. For those with free hearts—sincere seekers not yet believing but also not biased—the book provided the missing evidence they sought, leading them from confusion to the certainty of faith, based on rational proofs rather than emotional appeals. Notably, these included former proponents of dialectical materialism and atheism.

Why Desires Cannot Replace Rational Evidence
Buti critiques those who prioritize desires over reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational arguments are futile for someone who has subordinated reason to their desires, and why such a person cannot honestly admit this subordination.

Core Idea
Reason cannot reach a mind already captive to desires.

In this passage, Buti identifies a type of reader whose intellectual life is ruled by personal desire rather than objective evidence. He explains that for such a person, his book is a futile attempt, and why that person cannot be honest about their own position. This is a crucial insight into the limits of rational persuasion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the author's tone and the logic of his argument.
Notice how Buti uses contrast: people who put desires first vs. rational values.
2
Identify the target audience
Look for the description: those who place psychological desires first in their intellectual life. Understand why the author singles them out.
This group is contrasted with those who genuinely seek truth.
3
Understand the futility claim
The author says rational arguments are useless for this person because they have already completely subordinated reason to their desires. Reflect on why that makes dialogue impossible.
Consider: can you convince someone who has already decided that their wishes override any evidence?
4
See the psychological barrier
Buti notes that such a person cannot be frank about their subordination. If they did, the whole irrational stance would collapse. Why would admitting the truth destroy their position?
This reveals a kind of self-deception or bad faith.
5
Apply the lesson
Think about how this insight applies to debates today. When does rational argument become pointless? How can we identify when someone has prioritized desires over reason?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أناس آخرون يضعون رغباتهم النفسية في المكان الأول من حياتهم الفكرية والعقلية ، فلا ريب أن هذا الكتاب كان بالنسبة إليهم محاولة عقيمة ، ذلك لأن الذي يضع القيم العقلية والعلمية المجردة من حياته في الدرجة الثانية أو الثالثة ، لا يجدي معه التعامل بشيء من هذه القيم . بل من العبث أن تشدّه إليها وهو قد أخضعها إخضاعاً كاملاً لرغباته و سابق تطلعاته وآماله .. ومن الطبيعي أن أحداً من هؤلاء ، لا يصارحك بصنيعه هذا ، إذ لو فعل ذلك لم يبق لإخضاعه العقل ذلك الإخضاع أي قيمة أو معنى
As for other people who place their psychological desires in the first place in their intellectual and rational life, no doubt this book was for them a futile attempt. Because one who places abstract rational and scientific values in his life in the second or third degree, dealing with any of these values is of no use to him. Rather, it is futile to draw him to them when he has completely subordinated them to his desires and prior aspirations and hopes. And it is natural that none of these people will be frank with you about this, because if they did so, that subordination of reason would retain no value or meaning.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage identifies a category of people who prioritize their desires over rational inquiry. The author argues that for such individuals, rational arguments are futile because they have already subordinated reason to their wishes. Moreover, these people do not openly admit this subordination, because doing so would expose the irrationality of their position. This is a psychological and epistemological critique of bad faith.

Silence as Powerful Evidence
Author interprets silent reaction as proof of truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author considers the silence of critics after evasion as the greatest proof of his book's truth.

Core Idea
Silence after maneuvering is the strongest admission of truth.

In this brief but telling passage, the author reflects on a specific reaction to his book: silence. He interprets this not as a lack of response, but as an eloquent proof of the truth he presents. This lesson explores how the inability to refute arguments becomes evidence itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English to grasp the author's claim about silence.
Notice the repetition of 'silence' for emphasis.
2
Identify the author's argument
The author says silence after maneuvering is the greatest proof of truth. Why?
3
Reflect on the phrase 'speaking proof'
How can silence be a 'speaking proof'? Consider the logic: inability to refute implies truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كثير من هؤلاء الناس كانوا يواجهون هذا الكتاب ، بعد مرحلة من المناورة ، بالوجوم .. الوجوم فقط ..!! وإني لأعتقد أن هذا الوجوم ليس إلا أعظم دليل على الحق الذي ألفت كتابي هذا لبيان المزيد من دلائل وضوحه . وحسبنا من هؤلاء الناس أن ينتهوا إلى هذا الوجوم ثم يقفوا عنده .. إنه أبلغ تعبير عن حقيقة حالهم وواقع عذرهم .. فحسبنا أن تكون حالهم الصامتة هذه دليلاً ناطقاً لغيرهم .
Many of these people, after a phase of maneuvering, faced this book with silence... silence only!! And I believe that this silence is nothing but the greatest proof of the truth for which I authored this book to clarify more proofs of its clarity. Sufficient for us from these people is that they end in this silence and then stop at it. It is the most eloquent expression of the reality of their state and the actuality of their excuse. So sufficient for us is that this silent state of theirs is a speaking proof for others.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific reaction: silence after initial evasion. The author interprets this silence not as indifference but as the strongest evidence for the truth he presents. The inability to refute the arguments, even after attempting to maneuver, shows that the evidence is compelling. This silence becomes an implicit admission and serves as a lesson for others who seek the truth.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The silence of critics after evasion is a powerful indicator of the truth of the arguments presented.

Silence as Speaking Proof
The author interprets the silence of some readers as a powerful testimony to the truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author considers the silence of critics as a powerful testimony to the truth and how it functions as a proof.

Core Idea
Silence after maneuvering is the strongest proof of truth.

In this passage, the author reflects on the reaction of some readers who, after attempting to find fault, fall silent. He interprets this silence not as indifference but as the greatest proof of the truthfulness of his arguments. Let's see how he builds this compelling point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the emotional weight of the phrase 'silence only!!'.
2
Understand the context of maneuvering
The author mentions 'after a stage of maneuvering'. This implies that the readers have already tried to find faults or objections. Their silence comes after an attempt to refute.
Maneuvering indicates active opposition, not passive disinterest.
3
Identify the key claim
The author explicitly states that this silence is 'the greatest proof of the truth'. Find that sentence in the Arabic and note the confidence of the assertion.
The phrase 'أعظم دليل' (the greatest proof) is crucial.
4
Reflect on the implication
The author argues that the silence itself becomes a 'speaking proof' for others. Why does he say that? Think about how an inability to respond can be more telling than a weak response.
This connects to the idea that truth is self-evident when opposition falls silent.

And it suffices us from these people that they end up at this silence and then stop at it.. It is the most eloquent expression of the reality of their state and the truth of their excuse.. Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage explains the reaction of some readers who, after attempting to find fault, fall silent. The author considers this silence the greatest proof of the truth of his arguments, because their inability to respond reveals that they have no valid refutation. The silence itself becomes a 'speaking proof' for others to see.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author is claiming that silence always indicates agreement or that it is a universal proof of truth in any context.
Correction: The author specifies that this silence occurs 'after a stage of maneuvering,' meaning the opponents have already tried to refute and failed. It is their inability to respond after active opposition that makes the silence a proof, not mere quietness.

The silence of critics after they have tried and failed to refute is itself a powerful, speaking proof of the truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Skeptic's Doubt of Reason
The author refutes the claim that reason is unreliable by showing the inconsistency of the claimants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming to doubt reason is self-refuting based on the skeptic's own behavior.

Core Idea
Skepticism of reason is self-defeating because skeptics rely on reason to live and think.

This passage tackles a common objection: that reason cannot be trusted. The author, through a simple observation of human behavior, reveals the inconsistency of such a stance. By examining how skeptics actually live and argue, we see that they cannot avoid relying on the very faculty they claim to doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
Pay attention to the logical progression from objection to refutation.
2
Identify the skeptic's claim and behavior
The skeptic claims they need proof that reason is reliable. The author points out that they already rely on reason in daily life and intellectual pursuits.
Notice the explicit examples: daily life, philosophical principles, and the sudden rejection when facing faith.
3
Grasp the reductio ad absurdum
If someone truly rejects reason entirely, they cannot function—society calls them mad. The author concludes that such a person is excused from rational debate.
This is the logical punchline: consistent skepticism reduces to madness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبعض من هؤلاء كانوا يواجهونه أخيراً، بإعلان شكوكهم في أحكام العقل جملة!. فهم مفتقرون ـ فيما يزعمون - إلى ما يثبت لهم أن أحكام العقل لا خداع فيها
·
وجواب هؤلاء واضح بين، تستطيع أن تنتزعه بسهولة من واقع سلوكهم وحياتهم .
إن الذي لا يطمئن إلى أحكام العقل لا يقيم حياته المعيشية وعلاقاته الدنيوية المختلفة مع الآخرين على أدق إيحاءات العقل وأحكامه؛ وإن الذي لا يطمئن إلى أحكام العقل يقيم حياته الفكرية على مبادئ فلسفية مختلفة زاعماً أنه قد اتبع فيها بصيرة العقل ودلائل العلم . إن الذي لا يطمئن إلى أحكام العقل، لا يتعامل معه في كل مصالحه وشؤونه السلوكية المختلفة، حتى إذا رأى نفسه وجهاً لوجه مع دلائل الإيمان بالله وتوابعه أعلن فجأة عن عدم اطمئنانه إلى العقل، وقاطع العقل قائلاً: لا أعرفك ولا أتعامل معك !!
إن الذي لا يطمئن إلى أحكام العقل ولا يرى خيراً في اتباعه، إنما هو رجل قاطع العقل خلال رحلته الدنيوية جملة.. فهو لا يسترشد به في إقامة معيشة أو اقتناص مصلحة أو تخطيط سلوك.. ومثل هذا الإنسان يقال عنه في اصطلاح الناس كلهم « مجنون »! ومثل هذا الإنسان يقبل الدين معذرته ويضعها على العين والرأس؛ وليبتعد عن حقائق الكون ما طاب له الابتعاد وليكفر بها ما وسعه الكفر. فإنما هو مجنون، وليس على المجنون حرج .
And some of these would finally face it by announcing their doubts about the judgments of reason entirely! They are in need – as they claim – of something that proves to them that the judgments of reason are not deceptive.
·
And the answer to these is clear and evident; you can easily extract it from the reality of their behavior and life.
Indeed, he who does not trust the judgments of reason does not establish his daily life and his various worldly relations with others on the most precise inspirations and judgments of reason; and indeed, he who does not trust the judgments of reason establishes his intellectual life on various philosophical principles, claiming that he has followed in them the insight of reason and the proofs of science. Indeed, he who does not trust the judgments of reason does not deal with it in all his interests and various behavioral affairs, until when he finds himself face to face with the proofs of faith in God and its consequences, he suddenly announces his lack of trust in reason, and cuts off reason saying: 'I do not know you and I do not deal with you!!'
Indeed, he who does not trust the judgments of reason and sees no good in following it, he is a man who has cut off reason entirely during his worldly journey.. So he is not guided by it in establishing a livelihood, or seizing an interest, or planning behavior.. Such a person is called in the terminology of all people 'madman'! And such a person, religion accepts his excuse and places it upon the eye and the head; so let him distance himself from the realities of the universe as he pleases, and let him disbelieve in them as much as he can. For he is a madman, and there is no blame on the madman.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation. The objection is that some readers claim the judgments of reason are untrustworthy, so rational proof of God's existence is invalid. The author refutes by pointing to their own behavior: they rely on reason in daily life and in constructing their own philosophical systems. They only reject reason when it leads to faith. The argument culminates in a reductio ad absurdum: if someone truly rejects reason entirely, they become like a madman, and religion excuses such a person. This shows the inconsistency of the objection.

Key Terms
أحكام العقل
مجنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is simply calling all skeptics mad.
Correction: The author uses a reductio to show that if someone truly rejected reason entirely, they would be functionally mad; he does not claim actual skeptics are mad, but that their position is inconsistent.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute those who claim to doubt the judgments of reason?
A) By quoting scripture.
B) By showing they rely on reason in daily life.
C) By accusing them of madness outright.
D) By offering new proofs.

Key Takeaway
The claim that reason is unreliable is self-refuting because those who make it rely on reason in their daily lives and intellectual pursuits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a clear truth because it demanded a change in your life? When did you last use reason to advance your career but ignore it when it pointed to your need for Allah?
?
If reason is a gift from Allah to guide you, are you using it fully in your journey to Him, or do you selectively turn it off when it confronts your desires?
?
The skeptic in this passage is exposed as inconsistent. Where in your own life do you claim to follow reason but then ignore it when it comes to matters of faith?

Understanding the Author's Revisions in the New Edition
The author explains the revisions made in the new edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main improvements the author made in the new edition and why he edited certain sentences.

Core Idea
The author revises for clarity, not to change his core arguments.

This passage provides insight into the author's methodology. He explains that he did not radically alter the book's content but focused on improving clarity and precision. We see how he addressed complexity in technical discussions and added detail on dialectical materialism, while also refining language to avoid any misrepresentation of God's perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the author's intent. Notice that he begins with a question.
The passage is a methodological note, not an argument.
2
Identify the two main changes
The author lists two improvements: simplifying discussions on 'dalalat al-iltizam' and 'qiyas', and adding detail on dialectical materialism. Note why he made these changes.
He also mentions editing unclear or inappropriate sentences.
3
Understand the reason for editing sentences
The author changed sentences that were unclear, could imply something unworthy of God, or deviated from scientific investigation. This shows his commitment to precision and respect.
He credits brother readers for observations.
4
Reflect on the overall purpose
The author seeks more clarity and disclosure of truth without changing core content. This reflects a careful scholarly approach.
The passage ends mid-sentence; we infer that he appreciates feedback.

هل غيرتُ شيئاً من بحوث الكتاب أو زدت عليها ؟
لم أتناول شيئاً من مضمون الكتاب بأي تغيير جذري، ولكنني قمت بتحقيق أمرين اثنين ابتغاء المزيد من الوضوح، والمزيد من الكشف عن الحقيقة

ولكني بالإضافة إلى ذلك غيرت بعض الجمل والكلمات التي لم تكن ذات دلالة واضحة على معانيها المقصودة . أو التي كانت توهم أموراً لا تليق - من الناحية الشكلية والأدبية أو من الناحية الموضوعية - بكمال الله تعالى وألوهيته، أو التي تتضمن جنوحاً عن التحقيق العلمي المطلوب
وأكثر هذه الجمل التي غيرتها، إنما هو بفضل إخوة مؤمنين لم يضنوا علي بملاحظاتهم التي
Did I change anything from the researches of the book or add to it?
I did not touch anything of the content of the book with any radical change, but I accomplished two things seeking more clarity and more disclosure of the truth.
·
First: Simplifying some points included in the methodology of the search for truth; for I had sensed in them some complexity and that was confirmed to me from observations received from some brother readers. So I expanded the discussion on how 'concomitant signification' (dalalat al-iltizam) and 'signification of syllogism based on the cause' (dalalat al-qiyas al-qa'im 'ala al-'illa) and I removed the discussion as much as possible from the circle of dry technical terms and scientific methods, and I opened the horizons of their relation to human thought with more diverse examples related to various aspects of life.
Second: Presenting more detail about dialectical materialism and its scientific value, within the context of the investigation of the proofs of the existence of God Almighty. This is the detail that I had missed presenting in the first edition.
But in addition to that, I changed some sentences and words that did not have a clear indication of their intended meanings. Or that suggested things that are not fitting – from the formal and literary aspect or from the objective aspect – with the perfection of God Almighty and His divinity, or that contained a deviation from the required scientific investigation.
And most of these sentences that I changed were due to believing brothers who did not withhold from me their observations which [incomplete].
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a methodological note on the revisions. The author states that he made no radical changes but two improvements. First, he simplified technical discussions on 'dalalat al-iltizam' (concomitant signification) and 'qiyas' (syllogism based on cause) by adding examples and avoiding dry terminology. Second, he added more detail on dialectical materialism in the section on proofs of God's existence. Additionally, he edited sentences that were unclear or could imply something unworthy of God's perfection. He credits believing brothers for their observations, though the sentence is incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author's edits indicate a retraction of his earlier views.
Correction: The author explicitly states he did not make any radical change to the content, only improvements for clarity.

Checkpoint

A) He completely rewrote the book.
B) He simplified the discussion of dalalat al-iltizam and qiyas.
C) He removed all references to materialism.
D) He added a new chapter on ethics.

Key Takeaway
The author revised his book to enhance clarity and precision without altering its core conclusions, demonstrating a commitment to scholarly improvement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a book or listen to a lecture that challenges your current understanding, are you eager to revise your views for greater clarity, or do you cling to familiar ideas even if they lack precision? What stops you from embracing correction?
?
The author welcomed feedback from readers to improve his work. Think of a time when someone pointed out an error or lack of clarity in your understanding of faith. How did you respond? Are you willing to admit you were wrong and refine your belief?
?
The author changed words that might unintentionally imply something unworthy of God. Examine your own speech and thoughts: Are there ways you speak about Allah that, if examined closely, fall short of His perfection? What will you do to correct that today?

Rejection of Reason Is Insanity
The author declares that rejecting reason in faith is insanity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author equates rejecting reason in matters of faith with insanity.

Core Idea
Abandoning reason in faith is not piety—it is madness.

In this passage, the author confronts a common but dangerous idea: that faith requires a suspension of reason. He argues that anyone who rejects rational proofs of God's existence is not a sincere skeptic but someone who has abandoned reason altogether. Such a person, in the eyes of all people, is considered insane. This lesson unpacks that bold claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and English translation carefully. Note the author's strong language: 'I do not know you and I do not deal with you'.
2
Analyze the syllogism
The author implies that anyone who rejects reason's judgments in worldly matters is called insane, and this person also rejects reason in faith, therefore they are insane. Note the logical structure.
The author uses a form of reductio ad absurdum.
3
Consider the implication
What does it mean for religion to 'accept his excuse'? The author says religion places the excuse on the eye and head, meaning the insane are not accountable, but this does not justify their disbelief.
This is a rhetorical move to show the absurdity of rejecting reason.
4
Reflect on the misconception
The common misunderstanding is that faith requires abandoning reason. The author argues the opposite: reason is essential, and its rejection is insanity.
Compare with other Islamic theological positions on reason and faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السلوكية المختلفة ، حتى إذا رأى نفسه وجهاً لوجه مع دلائل الإيمان بالله وتوابعه أعلن فجأة عن عدم اطمئنانه إلى العقل ، وقاطع العقل قائلاً : لا أعرفك ولا أتعامل معك !! إن الذي لا يطمئن إلى أحكام العقل ولا يرى خيراً في اتباعه ، إنما هو رجل قاطع العقل خلال رحلته الدنيوية جملة .. فهو لا يسترشد به في إقامة معيشة أو اقتناص مصلحة أو تخطيط سلوك .. ومثل هذا الإنسان يقال عنه في اصطلاح الناس كلهم « مجنون » ! ومثل هذا الإنسان يقبل الدين معذرته ويضعها على العين والرأس ؛ وليبتعد عن حقائق الكون ما طاب له الابتعاد وليكفر بها ما وسعه الكفر. فإنما هو مجنون ، وليس على المجنون حرج .
The different behaviors, until he finds himself face to face with the proofs of faith in God and its consequences, he suddenly declares his lack of confidence in reason, and cuts off reason saying: 'I do not know you and I do not deal with you!!' Indeed, the one who does not trust the judgments of reason and sees no good in following it is a man who has cut off reason entirely during his worldly journey.. So he does not seek guidance from it in establishing a livelihood, or seizing a benefit, or planning behavior.. And such a person is called in the terminology of all people 'insane'! And such a person, religion accepts his excuse and places it on the eye and the head; let him distance himself from the truths of the universe as much as he pleases, and let him disbelieve in them as much as he can. He is nothing but insane, and there is no blame on the insane.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical statement by the author about the necessity of reason in matters of faith. It begins by describing a person who, when confronted with proofs of God's existence and its corollaries, suddenly announces his distrust of reason and refuses to engage with it. The author then argues that such a person is actually someone who has abandoned reason entirely in his worldly life—not using it for livelihood, benefit, or planning. Therefore, in common terminology, everyone agrees that this person is 'insane'. The author then says that religion accepts his excuse (since the insane are not accountable) but he may continue to distance himself from the truths of the universe and disbelieve in them. The passage concludes by reinforcing that he is insane and there is no blame upon him. This is a strong polemic to emphasize that rejecting reason outright is not a valid intellectual position; it is simply madness.

Key Terms
العقل
مجنون
دلائل الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that true faith requires suspending or rejecting reason.
Correction: The author argues that rejecting reason entirely is not a valid intellectual stance but a sign of insanity. Reason is necessary to recognize the proofs of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the status of a person who rejects reason when faced with proofs of faith?
A) He is a wise skeptic
B) He is insane
C) He is a true believer
D) He is a philosopher

Key Takeaway
Rejecting reason in matters of faith is not a valid position; it is equivalent to insanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever avoided rationally examining your beliefs because it felt uncomfortable or unspiritual? What does this passage say about that avoidance?
?
If the author's test were applied to you—do you use reason in your daily work and decisions but discard it when it comes to matters of faith—what would the author say about your approach?
?
The author says the one who rejects reason is insane and excused, not a true believer. Have you ever excused your own lack of intellectual engagement with faith as 'just being spiritual'? How does this passage challenge that excuse?

The Three Branches of Criticism
Buti enumerates the three branches of criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main lines of criticism Buti identifies in his opponent's book.

Core Idea
Buti's opponent attacks faith from three angles: science, free will, and materialism.

Before responding in detail, Buti first lays out the structure of the criticism he received. He identifies three distinct branches in the opposing book, each attacking a different pillar of Islamic belief. This sets the stage for his subsequent refutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of branches
Find the part where Buti describes the three branches. Notice how he distinguishes them: first the religion-science conflict, second the predestination issue, third the dialectical materialist explanation.
The branches are numbered in the Arabic text.
2
Identify the core claim of each branch
For each branch, summarize the opponent's main claim in one sentence.
Buti is concise; he states the essence of each criticism.
3
Understand the purpose of enumeration
Ask: Why does Buti present these three branches explicitly? How does this help his overall response?
He is showing that the criticism is not new and that his book already addresses them.
