Modern Doubts and Their Shared Root
Buti traces modern doubts to the same sources as old ones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that modern ideological doubts like materialism and evolution share the same root causes as ancient doubts: partisanship and desires.

Core Idea
Modern doubts are not new; they spring from the same old human weaknesses.

In this passage, Sheikh Ramadan al-Buti draws a direct lineage between the doubts of past generations and those of today. He argues that despite their modern packaging — materialism, evolution, new philosophies — these doubts are nourished by the same sources: blind partisanship and unchecked desires. This lesson will help you see through the scientific claims to the real drivers behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Buti frames the relationship between old and new doubts.
The passage uses a rhetorical question at the end for effect.
2
Identify the 'mother' of all doubts
Buti says both old and new doubts come from one mother: partisanship and desires. Find this claim in the text.
3
List the modern doubts
The passage lists four modern doubts. Write them down: materialist theory, evolution, new schools of thought, fascination with scientific discoveries.
4
Examine the false scientific methods
Buti identifies three non-scientific methods: guesswork, intuition, inference. See how he says partisanship turned them into 'scientific scales'.
Consider why someone would accept weak evidence if it supports their desires.
5
Reflect on the lesson's application
Think of a modern ideological claim you've encountered. Can you trace it to partisanship or desires rather than solid proof?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم راح الزمن يمضي ، فإذا بنا اليوم أمام شبه من نوع جديد ، وإن كان واضحاً أنها تمت إلى الشبه التي خلت من قبلُ بنسب الأخوة المتينة ، إذ هما جميعاً إنما ينحدران من أم واحدة هي : العصبية التي تتحكم بالشخصية والنفس ، والشهوات التي تعصف بالفكر والعقل . وكانت هذه الشبه الجديدة ، هي ما بالنظرية المادية لأصل الأشياء ، وقصة يسمى التطور والنشوء ، والمذاهب الجديدة في تفسير الفكر والوجود ، والانبهار الذي تركته الاكتشافات العلمية في بعض الرؤوس . شبه لا هي يوجود لها أي سلطان في موازين العلم وبراهينه ، وإنما سلطانها منبعث من معين « التوسم » و « الحدس » و « الاسترداد » بيد أن عوامل العصبية والأهواء والأغراض ، قالت لهذه الأشياء الثلاثة : كوني موازين علمية يقينية ، فكانت كذلك؟..
Then time passed, and behold, today we are faced with doubts of a new kind, although it is clear that they are connected to the previous doubts by the bond of strong brotherhood, since both originate from one mother: partisanship that controls the personality and soul, and desires that batter thought and intellect. These new doubts are: the materialist theory of the origin of things, the story called evolution and development, the new schools in interpreting thought and existence, and the fascination that scientific discoveries have left in some minds. Doubts that have no authority in the scales of science and its proofs; rather their authority emanates from the wellspring of 'guesswork', 'intuition', and 'inference'. But factors of partisanship, passions, and interests said to these three things: 'Be scientific and certain scales', and so they became?!
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a classification and critique of modern doubts. Buti first states that time has passed and new doubts have appeared, but they share a common mother with old doubts: partisanship and desires. He then lists the specific modern doubts: materialist theory, evolution, new schools interpreting thought and existence, and fascination with scientific discoveries. He argues that these doubts have no genuine scientific authority; they rely on guesswork, intuition, and inference. However, due to partisanship and desires, these weak methods are presented as scientific and certain.

Key Takeaway
Modern ideological doubts are not new; they derive their apparent authority from non-scientific methods bolstered by partisanship and desires.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Buti says that modern doubts originate from partisanship and desires. Think of a belief you hold that is comfortable or popular. Is it possible that you hold it not because of evidence, but because it satisfies a desire or aligns with your social circle? Be honest: are you willing to investigate it with the same rigor you expect from others?
?
The passage warns that guesswork, intuition, and inference are often mistaken for scientific certainty. Recall a time you accepted an idea simply because it 'felt right' or was 'common sense'—without checking the facts. How might that tendency be influencing your view of some of today's most debated issues? What concrete step will you take this week to challenge one of your intuitive assumptions?
?
Buti lists the fascination with scientific discoveries as a source of modern doubt. Have you ever been so impressed by a scientific claim that you unconsciously gave it more weight than the clear texts of revelation? What is one area of your life where you must actively reassert the authority of divine guidance over the allure of modern science? Write down one specific action you will take to correct that imbalance.

Engaging with Doubts: A Methodological Imperative
Buti on engaging doubts using opponents' own criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that before debating truth, one must engage with doubts on their own terms using the criteria accepted by the opponent.

Core Idea
Meet doubts on their own ground before dismissing them.

Buti begins by addressing the proper attitude toward doubts. He insists that those who wish to guide others to truth must not mock or dismiss doubts, but rather examine them using the very standards the doubters themselves claim to accept. This lesson explores the first step of a sound methodology: taking doubts seriously enough to test them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the imperative tone: 'you must receive them', 'you must not mock'.
Buti uses strong language to emphasize the duty.
2
Identify the three possible outcomes
After placing doubts under the microscope, Buti says three things may be revealed: falsity of the doubts, falsity of their fabricators, or return to truth. List them.
3
Reflect on why mockery is forbidden
Buti explicitly says not to mock even contradictory appearances. Consider why mockery would be counterproductive in a methodological approach.
Mockery may harden positions and prevent honest examination.
4
Consider the broader method
Buti refers to what 'our predecessors' did: using pure science and reason according to the opponents' criteria. This is a key methodological principle.
This sets the stage for the next lesson on the vicious circle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن مهما يكن، فإن على من يريد أن يشير للناس إلى الحق، أن يناقش السبل والمشكلات التي تعرقل السبيل إليه، مهما كان شأن هذه الشبه والمشكلات من الضعف، ومهما كان يتجلى فيها معنى الاختلاق والزيف. إن عليك أن تستقبلها بالمظهر ذاته الذي تزعم أنها تقبل إليك فيه، ولو كان مظهر العلم واليقين. بل إن عليك أن لا تضحك مطلقاً المظهر هذا التخفي المتنكر مهما كان مظهراً متناقضاً أو طريفاً. إذا فإنَّ علينا أن نفعل ما فعله أسلافنا، فنضع هذه الشبه الجديدة تحت مجهر العلم والعقل المجرّدين طبقاً للموازين الفكرية التي يعتد بها أصحاب هذه الشبه، وسيكشف ذلك أخيراً إما عن زيف هذه الشبه أو عن زيف من يصطنعونها، أو عن رجوعهم إلى الحق والتحرر من الباطل. ولكن مهلاً.. فإن هذا أيضاً لا يكفي. إن النتيجة لا تعدو أن تدور (مع طائفة كبيرة من المستشكلين) في حلقة مفرغة... تضع أمام أحدهم الدين، فيطالبك بالدليل، وتقدم له الدليل فيقول إنه مأخوذ من الدين!.. وتبتعد عن الدين لتناجي فيه العقل والعلم وحده، فيقول لك إن العلم لا يؤمن إلا ببرهان التجربة والمشاهدة. فمن أجل ذلك نجد أن كل ما يكتبه معظم المدافعين عن الحق في جانب، ومعظم العقول المتحيزة أو الملحدة في جانب آخر ولا نجد أن شيئاً من تلك الأدلة والبراهين يتماسك عليها. فما السبب؟ السبب هو عدم وضع منهج كامل للبحث عن الحقيقة، قبل الدخول في أي مناقشة عن الحقيقة ذاتها. وهذا ما لا تجد منه شيئاً عند أصحاب الشبه ودعاتها. فكيف تطمع أن تسير مع أحدهم على صراط من العلم إلى الحق الذي يكمن في نهايته، إذا لم يكن لديه أي خارطة عن هذا الصراط ولا أي علم عن مراحله ومنعطفاته؟ والعجيب حقاً أن نجد ثلة ممن درسوا من كل فن جانباً ثم زعموا أنهم تخصصوا في الفلسفة والمنطق وطرائق البحث - يفصلون القول في كثير من حقائق العقيدة عن الأنبياء واليوم الآخر كما يتخيلون ويحبون، دون أن يركبوا إلى شيء من ذلك متن أي طريقة في البحث، بل تجدهم يقفزون إلى ذلك قفزاً وقد أغمضوا أعينهم وأفكارهم، فما يدري أحدهم أهو ينحط في متاهات من الجهل أم وسط ساحات من التخيل والحدس!
However, regardless [of that], whoever wants to guide people to the truth must discuss the paths and problems that obstruct the way to it, no matter how weak these doubts and problems are, and no matter how much the meaning of fabrication and falsity is manifest in them. You must receive them with the very appearance in which they claim to come to you, even if it is the appearance of science and certainty. Rather, you must absolutely not mock this disguised appearance, no matter how contradictory or odd it appears. So then we must do what our predecessors did: place these new doubts under the microscope of pure science and reason, according to the intellectual criteria acknowledged by the proponents of these doubts, and that will ultimately reveal either the falsity of these doubts or the falsity of those who fabricate them, or their return to the truth and liberation from falsehood. But wait... this is also not sufficient. The result cannot but rotate (with a large group of questioners) in a vicious circle... You present religion to one of them, and he demands proof from you, and when you present the proof, he says it is taken from religion!... And you distance yourself from religion to address him through reason and science alone, and he says to you that science believes only in the proof of experiment and observation. That is why we find that everything written by most defenders of the truth is on one side, and most biased or atheist minds are on the other side, and we find that none of those proofs and arguments hold up against them. So what is the cause? The cause is the failure to establish a complete methodology for the search for truth, before entering into any discussion about truth itself. And you find nothing of this with the proponents of doubts and their advocates. How can you hope to walk with one of them on a path of science to the truth that lies at its end, if he has no map of this path and no knowledge of its stages and turns? And it is truly strange that we find a group of those who have studied something of every art and then claimed to specialize in philosophy, logic, and methods of inquiry - they expound at length on many truths of creed concerning prophets and the Last Day according to their imagination and desire, without mounting any method of inquiry for any of that. Rather, you find them leaping into that, having closed their eyes and minds, so that none of them knows whether he is descending into labyrinths of ignorance or into arenas of imagination and conjecture!
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the necessary methodological foundation for successful theological debate. Buti begins by stating that one must engage with opponents' doubts on their own terms, using the very standards they claim to accept—even if those standards are only spurious. He then transitions to the second point: that even this approach is insufficient because many skeptics operate in a vicious circle (حلقة مفرغة). When presented with religious proofs, they demand external proof; when presented with rational proofs, they demand empirical proof. The result is a stalemate. Buti identifies the root cause as the absence of a complete methodology (منهج كامل) for the search for truth. Without an agreed-upon method, every debate falls into confusion. He illustrates this by criticizing those who claim expertise in philosophy or logic but jump to conclusions without any methodological framework. The passage thus serves as a methodological warning: before debating specific theological truths, one must first ensure that the interlocutor shares a basic methodological commitment. Buti is not here providing a specific proof for a theological doctrine; rather, he is setting the epistemological conditions for fruitful dialogue.

Key Terms
الشبه
براهين
موازين فكرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Weak or fabricated doubts can be ignored or mocked.
Correction: Buti argues that even weak doubts must be engaged using the opponents' own criteria, because the outcome may reveal truth or falsehood, and mockery is prohibited.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what should one do when confronting a doubt that appears weak and fabricated?
A) Ignore it entirely.
B) Mock it to expose its weakness.
C) Examine it under the microscope using the criteria of its proponents.
D) Reject it because it is fabricated.

Key Takeaway
Engaging doubts on their own terms, using the criteria acknowledged by their proponents, is the first step in a sound methodology for seeking truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever brushed off a doubt about your faith because it seemed silly or weak, without truly engaging with it? Could your dismissal have been a form of intellectual pride that actually drives people away from the truth?
?
When you hear an argument that appears contradictory or absurd, what is your immediate reaction? Are you quick to mock, or do you pause to consider that the person presenting it might have a genuine concern that deserves a serious response?
?
What would it cost you to take a doubt seriously and examine it according to the objector’s own criteria—even if that doubt seems flimsy? Is there a specific doubt you have been avoiding? Will you commit to addressing it using Buti's method this week?

The Vicious Circle and the Need for a Complete Methodology
Buti on the vicious circle and methodological failure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why debates about truth often fail and why a complete methodology is necessary before any discussion.

Core Idea
Without a shared method, debate becomes a vicious circle.

Buti continues his argument by showing that even the careful engagement with doubts can lead to an impasse. He describes a vicious circle where skeptics demand proofs that are never acceptable to them. The root cause, he argues, is the absence of a complete methodology for the search for truth. This lesson unpacks that diagnosis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the vicious circle
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the circular reasoning Buti describes: when presented with religious proof, the skeptic demands external proof; when given rational proof, he demands empirical proof.
This circle leads to a stalemate.
2
Understand Buti's diagnosis
Buti asks 'What is the cause?' and answers: failure to establish a complete methodology before discussing truth. Note that he doesn't blame stubbornness.
Methodology is the key.
3
Reflect on the map metaphor
Buti compares methodology to a map for a journey. Without a map, one cannot navigate the path to truth. This illustrates the necessity of a prior framework.
4
Consider the criticism of pseudo-experts
Buti criticizes those who claim expertise in philosophy and logic but jump to conclusions about creed without any method. They are like people leaping with closed eyes.
This shows that even scholars can fall into error without a proper method.
5
Summarize the main point
Write one sentence summarizing why Buti says a complete methodology is essential before debating truth.
This will reinforce the learning objective.

Confronting Doubts on Their Own Terms
Buti outlines the method for addressing doubts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's methodology for addressing doubts: that they must be confronted seriously using the very standards the doubter claims to follow, rather than dismissed or ridiculed.

Core Idea
Face doubts with their own claimed appearance, not with ridicule.

Buti addresses a common mistake: dismissing weak or fabricated doubts. He argues that the one guiding people to truth must engage every obstacle, no matter how trivial it seems. The key is to meet doubts on their own terms, using the intellectual standards the doubter accepts. This approach, practiced by early scholars, either exposes the doubt's falsity or leads the doubter back to truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the rhetorical emphasis on 'however weak' and 'however fabricated'.
2
Identify the three-part instruction
Find the three parts: the duty to engage, the manner of engagement (using the opponent's standards), and the expected outcome.
Buti uses 'إن عليك أن...' for the manner.
3
Reflect on the method's effectiveness
Consider why using the opponent's own standards makes the argument compelling. How does this differ from simply dismissing doubts?
This connects to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن مهما يكن ، فإن على من يريد أن يشير للناس إلى الحق ، أن يناقش السبل والمشكلات التي تعرقل السبيل إليه ، مهما كان شأن هذه الشبه والمشكلات من الضعف ، ومهما كان يتجلى فيها معنى الاختلاق والزيف . إن عليك أن تستقبلها بالمظهر ذاته الذي تزعم أنها تقبل إليك فيه ، ولو كان مظهر العلم واليقين . بل إن عليك أن لا تضحك مطلقاً المظهر هذا التخفي المتنكر مهما كان مظهراً متناقضاً أو طريفاً
إذا فإنَّ علينا أن نفعل ما فعله أسلافنا ، فنضع هذه الشبه الجديدة تحت مجهر العلم والعقل المجردين طبقاً للموازين الفكرية التي يعتد بها أصحاب هذه الشبه ، وسيكشف ذلك أخيراً إما عن زيف هذه الشبه أو عن زيف من يصطنعونها ، أو عن رجوعهم إلى الحق والتحرر من الباطل
But whatever the case, whoever wants to point people to the truth must discuss the paths and problems that obstruct the way to it, however weak these doubts and problems may be, and however much the meaning of fabrication and falsehood may appear in them. You must receive them with the very appearance with which they claim to come to you, even if it is the appearance of knowledge and certainty. Rather, you must not at all laugh at this disguised concealment, however contradictory or odd it may be. So we must do what our predecessors did: place these new doubts under the microscope of pure science and reason, according to the intellectual standards that the proponents of these doubts acknowledge. That will finally reveal either the falsity of these doubts or the falsity of those who fabricate them, or their return to the truth and liberation from falsehood.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a methodological instruction for addressing doubts against religious truth. Buti begins by asserting that whoever seeks to guide people to truth must engage with the obstacles that block the path, regardless of how weak or clearly fabricated those obstacles are. The key point is that one should not dismiss doubts based on their apparent weakness; rather, one must confront them with the very appearance they present, even if that appearance falsely claims to be scientific or certain. Buti warns against ridiculing these doubts, no matter how contradictory or strange they seem, because ridicule is not an effective refutation. Instead, the proper method, as practiced by early Muslim scholars, is to subject these doubts to rigorous analysis using the intellectual standards accepted by those who raise them. By doing so, the outcome will ultimately expose either the falsity of the doubts themselves, the dishonesty of their proponents, or lead the proponents back to the truth. The commentary follows Buti's logical flow: first establishing the obligation to engage, then the manner of engagement (using the opponent's own standards), and finally the expected result.

Correction: Buti insists that even weak or fabricated doubts must be addressed seriously using the standards of the doubter.

What method does Buti prescribe for dealing with doubts against religious truth?
A) Ignore them because they are weak.
B) Mock them to expose their absurdity.
C) Receive them with the appearance they present and examine them using the intellectual standards of those who raise them.
D) Reject them immediately without discussion.

Key Takeaway
Buti teaches that effective refutation requires engaging doubts on their own terms using the standards of those who raise them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Are you willing to do that, or are you afraid that your faith might not withstand scrutiny? Commit to looking into one doubt this week with the microscope of science and reason.
?
The text says 'you must not at all laugh at this disguised concealment, however contradictory or odd it may be.' Think of a time you mocked someone's doubt. How did that affect your ability to guide them? What will you do differently now to engage respectfully?

The Vicious Circle in Religious Debate
Buti identifies the vicious circle where skeptics demand evidence from religion and then reject it as being from religion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the vicious circle that skeptics create in debates about religious truth and why a shared methodology is necessary to break it.

Core Idea
Skeptics trap you in a cycle: demand proof from religion, then reject it as religious.

Buti exposes a common impasse in debates about religious truth. When you present religious evidence, skeptics demand proof; when you provide it, they claim it is derived from religion and thus invalid. If you switch to reason and empirical evidence, they insist on experimental proof. This leaves no common ground. Buti argues the root cause is the absence of a shared methodology for seeking truth. This lesson explores that cycle and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Observe the vicious circle
Read the passage carefully and identify the cycle: the skeptic demands proof, you give proof, he rejects it as religious; you use reason, he demands empirical proof. Notice how the goalposts keep moving.
This cycle is the central phenomenon Buti describes.
2
Recognize the consequence
Buti states that because of this cycle, arguments from both sides fail to cohere. The problem is not just stubbornness but a structural lack of common ground.
3
Identify the root cause
Buti diagnoses that there is no agreed-upon method for seeking truth before entering debate. Without a 'map' of the path, productive discussion is impossible.
The lack of a complete methodology is the key issue.
4
Reflect on the solution
Think about what a 'complete methodology' might entail. How could one establish common epistemological ground before tackling specific claims?
This sets up the next part of Buti's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن مهلاً .. فإن هذا أيضاً لا يكفي .
إن النتيجة لا تعدو أن تدور ( مع طائفة كبيرة من المستشكلين ) في حلقة مفرغة ... تضع أمام أحدهم الدين ، فيطالبك بالدليل ، وتقدم له الدليل فيقول إنه مأخوذ من الدين !.. وتبتعد عن الدين لتناجي فيه العقل والعلم وحده ، فيقول لك إن العلم لا يؤمن إلا ببرهان التجربة والمشاهدة
فمن أجل ذلك نجد أن كل ما يكتبه معظم المدافعين عن الحق في جانب ، ومعظم العقول المتحيزة أو الملحدة في جانب آخر ولا نجد أن شيئاً من تلك الأدلة والبراهين يتماسك عليها .
فما السبب ؟ السبب هو عدم وضع منهج كامل للبحث عن الحقيقة ، قبل الدخول في أي مناقشة عن الحقيقة ذاتها . وهذا ما لا تجد منه شيئاً عند أصحاب الشبه ودعاتها . فكيف تطمع أن تسير مع أحدهم على صراط من العلم إلى الحق الذي يكمن في نهايته ، إذا لم يكن لديه أي خارطة عن هذا الصراط ولا أي علم عن مراحله ومنعطفاته ؟
But wait... this too is not sufficient. The result is that it revolves (with a large group of questioners) in a vicious circle... You present religion to one of them, and he demands proof; you present him the proof, and he says it is taken from religion! And you move away from religion to address him with reason and science alone, and he tells you that science believes only in the proof of experiment and observation. Because of that, we find that everything written by most defenders of the truth is on one side, and most biased or atheist minds are on the other side, and we find that none of those proofs and evidences hold together. So what is the cause? The cause is the failure to establish a complete methodology for seeking truth before entering into any discussion about truth itself. And you find none of this with the proponents of doubts and their advocates. So how can you hope to walk with one of them on a path of science to the truth that lies at its end, if he has no map of this path and no knowledge of its stages and turns?
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage identifies a fundamental obstacle in debates about religious truth: the vicious circle. Buti describes a typical exchange: when you present religious arguments, the skeptic demands proof; when you provide it, he claims it is derived from religion and therefore invalid. If you then abandon religious premises and appeal to pure reason and science, he insists that science only accepts empirical proof. This circular reasoning leaves no common ground, causing both sides to talk past each other. Buti observes that most arguments on both sides fail to cohere because of this lack of shared methodology. The root cause, he argues, is the absence of an agreed-upon method for searching for truth before delving into specific questions. Without a shared 'map' of the path to truth, productive discussion is impossible. The commentary follows Buti's argument: first presenting the problem, then its consequence (futile arguments), then the diagnosis (no common methodology).

Key Terms
حلقة مفرغة
برهان التجربة والمشاهدة
منهج كامل
خارطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The problem in debates is simply that skeptics are stubborn.
Correction: Buti argues the deeper issue is the absence of a shared methodology for seeking truth, not just stubbornness.

Checkpoint
What is the 'vicious circle' that Buti describes?
A) Defenders of truth keep repeating the same arguments.
B) Skeptics demand religious proof but reject it as being from religion, and when you use reason, they demand empirical proof.
C) Both sides continuously talk but never reach a conclusion.
D) The arguments are too complex for ordinary people to understand.

Key Takeaway
Productive debate about religious truth requires a shared methodological framework before addressing specific claims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt frustrated in a debate because your evidence was dismissed? How does Buti's diagnosis of the vicious circle reveal that the real issue might have been the lack of a shared foundation—and what will you do differently next time?
?
When you present Islam to others, do you assume that providing proofs will be enough? How does this passage challenge you to reconsider your approach? Commit to establishing a common methodology before arguing.
?
The root cause is the absence of a complete methodology for truth-seeking. In your own search for truth, do you have a clear map? If not, what is the first step you will take today to develop one?

The Necessity of Methodology Before Creed
Buti argues for methodological rigor and outlines his book's structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti insists on a shared method of inquiry before any debate about creed, and how this shapes his book's structure.

Core Idea
Before debating truth, we must agree on the method of seeking it.

Buti opens his work by emphasizing that without a shared methodology, theological discourse descends into confusion between certainties, conjectures, and illusions. He presents a stark choice: either religion is mere blind belief, or it is grounded in certainty. His book's entire structure is designed to prove the latter and expose the fallacy of those who leap to conclusions without method.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the rhetorical force of the conditional 'if... then' structure.
2
Identify the two possible outcomes
Buti presents two possibilities: either the 'jumpers' are correct (religion is mere belief) or they are wrong. Trace how he responds to each.
The 'jumpers' are those who reject religious certainty without rigorous method.
3
Understand the role of methodology
Buti says we must first 'reveal the method of research' so that certainties are not confused with conjectures or illusions. Ask yourself: why is this step necessary before any proof?
Without method, arguments become muddled.
4
Follow the book plan
Buti lists three main parts: a detailed preface on method, a preface on humanity's need for creed, and then four sections on divine matters, prophecies, cosmic matters, and unseen matters.
Notice the logical progression: method → need → content.
5
Reflect on the personal motivation
Buti mentions that these ideas came to him while teaching at Damascus University. How does this personal context strengthen his argument?
It grounds the work in real pedagogical challenges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل ذلك لا بد قبل البحث في مقومات العقيدة الإسلامية وبراهينها ، من الكشف عن منهج البحث إلى ذلك كي لا تلتبس اليقينيات بالظنيات أو الوهميات . ولكي نعلم : هل حقاً أن منبع الدين في نفوسنا هو مجرد الاعتقاد على حين أن منبعه في أفكار أولئك « الوثابين » هو العلم والبرهان
فإن رأينا أن الأمر كذلك ، أي كما يقولون ، فإن علينا أن نبادر فنتخلص من عقيدة لا شأن لها في حياتنا إلا أن تسترق عقولنا وتبعدنا عن ساحة العلم واليقين . وإن رأينا الأمر بالعكس أوضحنا لمن يتقنون حركة القفز والوثب أن هذه الحركة وإن لم تكسر رجل صاحبها أو تدق عنقه فإنها على كل حال لا يمكن أن تنقلب إلى برهان وعلم .
طاف بذهني هذا كله وأنا أدرّس العقيدة الإسلامية في جامعة دمشق ولما دعتني الظروف إلى كتابة هذه المباحث : جعلت من هذه الأفكار مخططاً للبحث . فرأيت أن أبدأ
أولاً بكتابة تمهيد مفصل عن منهج البحث عن الحقيقة بين الفكر الإسلامي والفكر الغربي بل رأيت أن كل عملي وبحثي لا يأتي بطائل إن لم يقم من وراء هذا التمهيد الهام .
أتبعه بتمهيد آخر أوضح فيه حاجة الإنسان إلى عقيدة صادقة صحيحة عن الكون والحياة ، ثم إلى التزام معنى العبودية لواجب الوجود جل جلاله ، وأبين الرابطة بين وجود الله عز وجل وضرورة تقيد الإنسان بمنهج معين من الفكر والسلوك ؟
ورأيت أن أبدأ بعد ذلك ، كما فعل كثير من الباحثين من قبل ، فأقسم مباحث
العقيدة إلى أربعة أقسام :
الإلهيات ، والنبوات ، والكونيات ، والغيبيات .
Because of that, before researching the constituents of the Islamic creed and its proofs, it is necessary to reveal the method of research to it, so that certainties are not confused with conjectures or illusions. And so that we may know: Is it truly that the source of religion in our souls is mere belief, while its source in the thoughts of those 'jumpers' is science and proof? If we see that it is so, as they say, then we must hasten to rid ourselves of a creed that has no concern in our lives except to enslave our minds and distance us from the field of science and certainty. And if we see the opposite, we explain to those who master the movement of jumping and leaping that this movement, even if it does not break its owner's leg or break his neck, cannot in any case turn into proof and science. All this occurred to me while I was teaching Islamic creed at the University of Damascus, and when circumstances called me to write these discussions, I made these ideas a plan for research. So I saw that I should begin first by writing a detailed preface on the method of seeking truth between Islamic thought and Western thought; indeed, I saw that all my work and research would yield no benefit unless it was based on this important preface. I will follow it with another preface in which I clarify man's need for a truthful, correct creed about the universe and life, then for adherence to the meaning of servitude to the Necessary Existence, may His glory be exalted, and I will explain the link between the existence of God Almighty and the necessity of man's adherence to a specific method of thought and behavior. Then I saw that I should begin, as many researchers before me have done, by dividing the discussions of creed into four sections: divine matters (ilāhiyyāt), prophecies (nubuwwāt), cosmic matters (kawniyyāt), and unseen matters (ghaybiyyāt).
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage serves as a methodological introduction and outline of the book. Buti begins by asserting the necessity of establishing a clear method of inquiry before entering into discussions of Islamic creed and its proofs. The purpose is to prevent confusion between certainties, conjectures, and illusions. He then poses a critical question: is the source of religion in our souls mere belief, as the 'jumpers' claim, while their own source is science and proof? He presents two possibilities: if the jumpers are correct, then we should abandon a religion that only enslaves minds; if they are wrong, we must demonstrate that their method of leaping cannot produce genuine proof. Buti then reveals his personal background: these reflections came to him while teaching Islamic creed at the University of Damascus, and they formed the plan for this book. His plan has three main steps: first, a detailed preface on the method of seeking truth comparing Islamic and Western thought; second, a preface on humanity's need for a correct creed and the link between God's existence and moral obligation; and third, a division of creed into four standard sections: ilāhiyyāt (divine matters), nubuwwāt (prophethood), kawniyyāt (cosmic matters), and ghaybiyyāt (unseen matters). The commentary follows Buti's logical flow: the need for method, the conditional choice, the personal motivation, and the structural outline.

Key Terms
يقينيات (yaqīniyyāt): certainties
ظنيات (ẓanniyyāt): conjectures
وهميات (wahmiyyāt): illusions
الإلهيات (al-ilāhiyyāt): divine matters
النبوات (al-nubuwwāt): prophecies
الكونيات (al-kawniyyāt): cosmic matters
الغيبيات (al-ghaybiyyāt): unseen matters
تمهيد (tamhīd): preface

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Buti is simply defending tradition without a rational basis.
Correction: Buti actually demands a rigorous shared method before any debate; he is not anti-rational but pro-method.

Checkpoint
What is the first step in Buti's plan for the book?
A) A detailed preface on the method of seeking truth between Islamic and Western thought.
B) A preface on man's need for a creed.
C) The division of creed into four sections.
D) A refutation of atheism.

Key Takeaway
Buti's method is to first establish a shared method of inquiry, then prove humanity's need for a true creed, and finally examine creed through four categories: divine, prophetic, cosmic, and unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Buti warns against confusing certainties with conjectures or illusions. Where in your own life have you treated a deep-seated opinion as a certainty, when it might actually be conjecture? What would it take to honestly re-examine it?
?
Consider Buti's conditional: if your religious beliefs were shown to be mere belief without proof, would you be willing to abandon them? What does your answer reveal about how you hold your creed?
?
Buti argues that a correct method is necessary before any investigation. Are you personally committed to seeking truth only through a rigorous method, or do you sometimes jump to conclusions? How can you adopt a more disciplined approach in your own learning?

Buti's Critique of Labeling Islamic Belief as Mere 'I'tiqad
Buti critiques the labeling of Islamic belief as mere i'tiqad and poses a logical dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's critique of the inversion of terms between Islamic methodology and the 'leapers' approach, and the logical dilemma he poses to force methodological clarity.

Core Idea
The 'leapers' claim science but dismiss Islamic belief as mere 'i'tiqad – Buti flips the dilemma.

Buti begins with astonishment at how the so-called 'leapers' (waththabin) describe their own approach as 'science' while reducing Islamic belief to mere 'i'tiqad. He then presents their distorted view of religious history, then juxtaposes the Islamic understanding. The heart of the passage is a logical dilemma: either their claim is true, and we must abandon our faith, or it is false, and their leap cannot become proof. This forces us to demand methodological clarity before any further discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the inversion of terms
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key contrast: the 'leapers' call their own approach 'science' (علم) and label Islamic belief as mere 'belief' (اعتقاد). Buti finds this astonishing.
Pay attention to the rhetorical tone: 'And more astonishing is that you find them...'
2
Understand the two contrasting descriptions of religion
Buti presents two accounts: the leapers' view of religion as evolving from soothsaying to prophethood, and the Islamic view of religion as based on belief. Compare these and ask: which one is more plausible?
The leapers' account is dismissive; the Islamic account is presented without defense here—the dilemma will decide.
3
Analyze the logical dilemma and its implications
Buti poses a dilemma: if the leapers are right, then we must abandon our faith as unscientific; if they are wrong, their leap cannot become proof. Work through both branches and see how this forces a methodological inquiry.
This is the core of the lesson: Buti is not taking sides yet, only showing the need for clear methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأعجب ، أن تجدهم فوق ذلك ، يعبرون عن قفزهم هذا ( بالعلم ) .. ويعبرون عن منطلق المسلمين ومنهجيتهم ( بالاعتقاد ) !.. فالدين في حقيقته العلمية عند هؤلاء ( الوثابين ( سلسلة فكرية بدأت في عصورها الأولى بالكهانة والتنجيم ، ثم ترقت إلى السحر ، ثم إلى النبوة التي امتصت كثيراً من التقاليد والإحيائيات فجعلت لها قداسة روحية معينة . أما الدين كما يعلمه أنبياؤه والمؤمنون به والباحثون في أدلته وبراهينه فهو قائم على مجرد ( الاعتقاد ) !.. من أجل ذلك لا بد قبل البحث في مقومات العقيدة الإسلامية وبراهينها ، من الكشف عن منهج البحث إلى ذلك كي لا تلتبس اليقينيات بالظنيات أو الوهميات . ولكي نعلم : هل حقاً أن منبع الدين في نفوسنا هو مجرد الاعتقاد على حين أن منبعه في أفكار أولئك « الوثابين » هو العلم والبرهان فإن رأينا أن الأمر كذلك ، أي كما يقولون ، فإن علينا أن نبادر فنتخلص من عقيدة لا شأن لها في حياتنا إلا أن تسترق عقولنا وتبعدنا عن ساحة العلم واليقين . وإن رأينا الأمر بالعكس أوضحنا لمن يتقنون حركة القفز والوثب أن هذه الحركة وإن لم تكسر رجل صاحبها أو تدق عنقه فإنها على كل حال لا يمكن أن تنقلب إلى برهان وعلم .
And more astonishing is that you find them, on top of that, describing this leap of theirs as 'science'.. and describing the starting point of Muslims and their methodology as 'belief'!.. Thus religion in its scientific reality according to these 'leapers' is an intellectual series that began in its early ages with soothsaying and astrology, then progressed to magic, then to prophethood which absorbed many traditions and revivals and gave them a certain spiritual sanctity. As for religion as known by its prophets, its believers, and researchers in its evidences and proofs, it is based on mere 'belief'!.. For that reason, before researching the components of Islamic creed and its proofs, it is necessary to uncover the methodology of research for that, so that certainties are not confused with conjectures or illusions. And so that we know: Is it truly that the source of religion in our souls is mere belief, while its source in the ideas of those 'leapers' is science and proof? If we find the matter to be so, i.e. as they say, then we must hasten to rid ourselves of a creed that has no role in our lives except to enslave our minds and distance us from the realm of science and certainty. And if we find the matter to be the opposite, we clarify to those who master the movement of leaping and jumping that this movement, even if it does not break its owner's leg or break his neck, in any case cannot turn into proof and science.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical critique and a methodological challenge. The author begins by expressing astonishment ('wa'l-a'jab) at how the 'leapers' (al-waththabin) – by which he refers to those who dismiss Islamic belief as mere 'i'tiqad while claiming their own approach is 'science' – invert the terminology. He then describes their view of the origin of religion as a series progressing from soothsaying to prophethood. In contrast, he states that religion as understood by its adherents is based on mere belief. He then declares the necessity of examining methodology to avoid confusion between certainties and conjectures. The core of the argument is a logical dilemma posed as a question: if it is true that religion's source is mere belief while theirs is science, then we should abandon our creed as it is enslaving and unscientific. But if the opposite is true, then their leap cannot be turned into proof and science. This sets up the need for methodological clarity before proceeding.

علم
يقينيات
ظنيات
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Buti is entirely dismissing Western thought or all non-Islamic approaches.
Correction: Buti is only critiquing a specific claim about the nature of religious belief and demanding methodological rigor. He is not rejecting all external perspectives, but questioning a particular inversion of terms.

Checkpoint

A) Either the leapers are correct and we should keep our faith, or they are wrong and we should adopt their method.
B) Either the leapers are correct and we must abandon our faith, or they are wrong and their leap cannot become proof.
C) Either religion is based on belief or on science; we must choose one.
D) Either the leapers are Muslims or they are not; we must decide.

Key Takeaway
Buti's challenge forces a methodological choice: either accept the leapers' claim and abandon Islamic faith, or reject it and expose their leap as unscientific.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone dismisses your faith as 'just belief' while claiming their own worldview is 'scientific,' how do you feel—defensive, insecure, or confident? Buti's dilemma demands you examine whether your faith is indeed based on proof or just custom. What is your honest answer before Allah?
?
The leapers claim that religion began as soothsaying and magic. Have you ever secretly doubted the intellectual credibility of your faith when confronted with such historical narratives? This lesson forces you to choose: either your faith is baseless and you should abandon it, or it is true and their leap is invalid. Which way does your life lean?
?
Buti says if the leapers are right, we must 'hasten to rid ourselves' of a creed that enslaves the mind. Does your heart tremble at that possibility, or do you passively brush it off? What real evidence do you hold that makes you certain Islam is from Allah, and are you willing to stake your eternity on it?

Method of Learning

Buti's Book Plan: Two Prefaces and Four Sections
Buti outlines his book plan with two prefaces and four creedal sections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti structures his work on Islamic creed, beginning with two essential prefaces and then dividing the subject into four thematic sections.

Core Idea
A solid creedal work needs methodological grounding before content.

Before diving into the content of Islamic creed, Buti explains his plan for the book. He emphasizes that his research would be fruitless without first establishing a sound methodology for seeking truth, comparing Islamic and Western thought. This lesson introduces that plan, which consists of two prefaces and four sections that cover divine matters, prophethood, cosmic matters, and the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read Buti's Arabic description of his book structure, then the English translation. Notice how he organizes his thoughts.
The Arabic is a continuous paragraph; follow the flow of his plan.
2
Identify the two prefaces
Find where he describes the first preface on methodology and the second on man's need for a true creed and servitude to God.
He considers the first preface crucial—without it, the rest is worthless.
3
List the four sections
He divides creed into Ilahiyyat, Nubuwwat, Kawniyyat, and Ghaybiyyat. Note what each section covers as he describes.
The order is deliberate: start with God, then prophets, then the cosmos, then the unseen.
4
Observe the methodological thread
Notice how each section is tied to his methodology: scientific proof from zero belief, comparison with modern theories like evolution, and chronological treatment of eschatology.
He aims to combine persuasion of ancient and modern thinkers.

طاف بذهني هذا كله وأنا أدرّس العقيدة الإسلامية في جامعة دمشق ولما دعتني الظروف إلى كتابة هذه المباحث : جعلت من هذه الأفكار مخططاً للبحث . فرأيت أن أبدأ أولاً بكتابة تمهيد مفصل عن منهج البحث عن الحقيقة بين الفكر الإسلامي والفكر الغربي بل رأيت أن كل عملي وبحثي لا يأتي بطائل إن لم يقم من وراء هذا التمهيد الهام . أتبعه بتمهيد آخر أوضح فيه حاجة الإنسان إلى عقيدة صادقة صحيحة عن الكون والحياة ، ثم إلى التزام معنى العبودية لواجب الوجود جل جلاله ، وأبين الرابطة بين وجود الله عز وجل وضرورة تقيد الإنسان بمنهج معين من الفكر والسلوك ؟ ورأيت أن أبدأ بعد ذلك ، كما فعل كثير من الباحثين من قبل ، فأقسم مباحث العقيدة إلى أربعة أقسام : الإلهيات ، والنبوات ، والكونيات ، والغيبيات . وأن أبدأ بالإلهيات ، فأعرض الدليل العلمي على وجود الخالق جل جلاله طبق المنهج الواضح في التمهيد بدءاً من نقطة الصفر في الاعتقاد ، بأسلوب يجمع بين إقناع قدامى المفكرين ومحدثيهم ، ثم أتحدث عن الصفات الإلهية بالتفصيل شارحاً ما يتعلق بكل منها مجيباً عن كل ما قد يرد عليها ثم أتحدث عن النبوات : فأشرح معنى النبي والرسول ، وخصائص الأنبياء ، ولا بد من الإفاضة في البحث عند شرح ظاهرة الوحي وتحليلها ومعنى المعجزات وحقيقتها ، وموقف العقل والعلم من كل منهما . فإذا انتقلت إلى البحث عن الكونيات ، تحدثت عن الإنسان والملائكة والجان وقانون السببية في الكون ، ولا بد من المقارنة عند ذلك بين حقيقة الإنسان وقصته كما يفصل القرآن فيها القول وكما ترى نظرية النشوء والتطور ، كما لا بد من التفصيل عند الحديث عن السببية والعلية في الكون تفصيلاً يجمع بين مقتضيات العلم وحاجة الإيضاح فإذا تحدثت عن الغيبيات ، بدأت بشرح معناها ، وذكرت القارئ بالمنهج العلمي للوصول إلى أمر يقيني بشأنها ، ثم أخذت أعددها الواحدة تلو الأخرى طبقاً للتسلسل الزمني ، أي بدءاً من أشراط الساعة ، فالموت ، فعذاب القبر ، فالحشر ، فالحساب فالميزان ، فالصراط ، فالجنة والنار ، راجياً أن يوفقني الله لحل كل مشكلة وردّ كل شبهة قـد تعترض سبيل البحث العلمي في شيء من ذلك .
All of this crossed my mind while I was teaching Islamic creed at Damascus University, and when circumstances called me to write these investigations, I made these ideas a plan for research. So I saw that I should first begin by writing a detailed preface on the methodology of searching for truth between Islamic thought and Western thought; indeed I saw that all my work and research would come to nothing if it were not built upon this important preface. I follow it with another preface in which I clarify man's need for a truthful correct creed about the universe and life, then for commitment to the meaning of servitude to the Necessary Existence (glory be to His majesty), and I explain the connection between the existence of God (mighty and majestic) and the necessity of man's adherence to a specific methodology of thought and behavior. And I saw that I should then begin, as many researchers before me did, dividing the topics of creed into four sections: Divine matters, Prophethood, Cosmic matters, and Unseen matters. And that I begin with Divine matters, presenting the scientific proof for the existence of the Creator (glory be to His majesty) according to the clear methodology in the preface, starting from point zero in belief, in a style that combines the persuasion of ancient and modern thinkers. Then I speak about the divine attributes in detail, explaining what relates to each of them and answering everything that might be raised against them. Then I speak about Prophethood: I explain the meaning of prophet and messenger, the characteristics of prophets, and it is necessary to elaborate in the research when explaining the phenomenon of revelation and its analysis, and the meaning of miracles and their reality, and the stance of reason and science towards each of them. Then if I move to research on Cosmic matters, I speak about man, angels, jinn, and the law of causality in the universe, and it is necessary at that point to compare between the reality of man and his story as the Quran details the discourse about it and as the theory of evolution and development sees it; likewise it is necessary to detail when speaking about causality and causation in the universe in a detail that combines the requirements of science and the need for clarification. Then if I speak about Unseen matters, I begin by explaining their meaning, and remind the reader of the scientific methodology for arriving at a certain matter regarding them, then I begin to enumerate them one after another according to chronological sequence, i.e. starting from the signs of the Hour, then death, then the punishment of the grave, then the resurrection, then the reckoning, then the balance, then the path, then Paradise and Hell, hoping that God will grant me success in solving every problem and refuting every doubt that might obstruct the path of scientific research in any of that.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is an outline of the book's structure. The author states that while teaching Islamic creed at Damascus University, circumstances led him to write this work, and he formulated a plan. The plan begins with a detailed methodological preface comparing Islamic and Western thought, which he considers essential. Then a second preface on man's need for a true creed and the link between God's existence and human obligation. After these prefaces, he divides the creed into four sections: Ilahiyyat (divine matters), Nubuwwat (prophethood), Kawniyyat (cosmic matters), and Ghaybiyyat (unseen matters). He then elaborates on the content of each section: starting with Ilahiyyat, he will present the scientific proof for God's existence from zero belief, followed by detailed discussion of divine attributes. Under Nubuwwat, he explains prophet/messenger, their characteristics, and delves into revelation and miracles. Under Kawniyyat, he discusses man, angels, jinn, and causality, comparing the Quranic account with evolution theory. Under Ghaybiyyat, he explains their meaning, reminds of the scientific methodology for certainty, and enumerates eschatological events chronologically, seeking God's help to solve problems and refute doubts.

Correction: Buti stresses the first preface as crucial (all work would be fruitless without it), and the order of sections follows a logical progression from God to prophets to cosmos to the unseen.

?
Buti's plan starts 'from point zero in belief' as if the reader had no faith. Are you willing to re-examine your belief with that kind of honesty? What would you have to let go of to truly start from zero?

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Two Methodological Commitments: Avoiding Speculative Theology and Sectarian Debates
Buti states his two commitments: avoiding discussion on divine attributes and avoiding extensive sectarian disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's two methodological commitments for writing his investigations: avoiding speculative theology on divine attributes and avoiding deep sectarian disputes.

Core Idea
Buti prioritizes essential faith over speculative theological debates.

In this passage, Buti lays out his methodology for the entire book. He wants to keep the focus on what is clear and essential for faith, avoiding discussions that lead nowhere or cause unnecessary sectarian divisions. This sets a pragmatic and focused tone for his theological approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the two commitments Buti lists.
2
Analyze the first commitment
Examine Buti's first commitment: refraining from debating the nature of divine attributes. Ask why he considers this futile.
3
Analyze the second commitment
Examine the second commitment: avoiding deep disputes with the Mu'tazila. Understand his justification that such disputes do not affect faith.
4
Synthesize the methodology
Consider how these two commitments together show Buti's focus on practical certainty and avoiding unnecessary theological speculation.
This will help you understand the overall approach of the book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد التزمت الأمور التالية في كتابة هذه البحوث : أولاً ـ الابتعاد عن الخوض في حقيقة الصفات الإلهية وتحليلها وهل هي عين الذات أم غيرها ، وما يترتب على كل منهما ، مكتفياً باتباع مذهب جمهور المسلمين في ذلك . إذ يسع المسلم العاقل أن لا يفكر في ذلك أصلاً وأن لا يلتزم إلا ما نسبه الله تعالى إلى نفسه من صفات الكمال، على أنه لا توجد ثمة أي شبهة في الإيمان بالله يتوقف ردها على الخوض في هذا البحث الذي لا طائل فيه . ثانياً . عدم التوغل في كثير من الخلافات التي قامت بين المعتزلة وجمهور المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة ، إذ هي أمور لا ينتهي الجزم فيها بأحد القولين إلى الكفر ، لقيام الشبهة والاحتمال في أدلتها؛ ثم هي لا تتعلق بأي شبه في الإيمان لأي فئة من الناس اليوم . فحسبنا في ذلك أن نتبنى ما اتفق عليه جمهور المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة بعد معرفة الدليل والبرهان .
And I have committed to the following matters in writing these investigations: Firstly, refraining from delving into the reality of the divine attributes and their analysis, and whether they are identical to the essence or other than it, and what follows from each, contenting myself with following the school of the majority of Muslims in that. For the intelligent Muslim can avoid thinking about that entirely and not commit himself except to what God Almighty has attributed to Himself of attributes of perfection, on the basis that there is no doubt in faith in God whose rebuttal depends on delving into this futile research. Secondly, not penetrating deeply into many of the disputes that arose between the Mu'tazila and the majority of Muslims from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, for they are matters in which being definitively certain of one of the two views does not reach disbelief, due to the existence of uncertainty and probability in their evidences; moreover, they are not related to any doubt in faith for any group of people today. So it suffices for us in that to adopt what the majority of Muslims from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a have agreed upon after knowing the evidence and proof.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of two methodological commitments. The author states two principles he adhered to in writing. First, he refrains from discussing the metaphysical nature of divine attributes (whether they are identical to God's essence or distinct) and follows the majority view. He justifies this by saying that a reasonable Muslim can avoid these speculations entirely and only affirm what God has attributed to Himself, because no doubt in faith depends on resolving this issue, which he calls futile. Second, he avoids delving into the historical disputes between the Mu'tazila and the Sunni majority, because even being certain of one position does not lead to disbelief due to the presence of valid doubt and probability in the arguments. Moreover, these disputes are irrelevant to contemporary faith issues. He says it is sufficient to adopt the consensus of the majority after knowing the evidence. This shows his pragmatic approach to theology, focusing on practical certainty.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Buti is dismissing the importance of all theological debate.
Correction: He specifically avoids only the issues that are not essential to faith and have no definitive proof, not all theological debate.

Key Takeaway
Buti's methodology prioritizes clear and essential faith over speculative theological debates and sectarian disputes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter theological debates that seem endless and confusing, do you feel a pull to engage deeply or do you step back? Can you honestly say your faith depends on resolving these issues? What would it cost you today to follow Buti's path and focus only on what God has clearly revealed?
?
Think of a time you argued with someone over a religious matter that brought division rather than clarity. Was that argument necessary for your faith? If Buti's words 'لا طائل فيه' (futile) applied to that debate, how would you now choose to spend that energy instead?
?
You claim to believe in God's attributes of perfection—but do you live as if you truly believe, or do you spend more time analyzing them than embodying them? Buti says the intelligent Muslim can avoid thinking about the nature of attributes entirely. Honestly, compared to your intellectual curiosity, how strong is your desire for practical faith? What will you change today?

Overview of the Book's Structure and Content
Author outlines the four main sections of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four-part structure of the book and the author's methodological approach starting from zero belief.

Core Idea
The author builds his case for Islamic belief starting from zero, using reason and science across four domains.

This passage is the author's own roadmap for the entire book. He clearly lays out the four major sections – divine matters, prophethoods, cosmic matters, and unseen matters – and explains his logical progression from one to the next. It's a bird's-eye view of the entire argument.

This is a methodological outline, not a detailed argument.

وأن أبدأ بالإلهيات ، فأعرض الدليل العلمي على وجود الخالق جل جلاله طبق المنهج الواضح في التمهيد بدءاً من نقطة الصفر في الاعتقاد ، بأسلوب يجمع بين إقناع قدامى المفكرين ومحدثيهم ، ثم أتحدث عن الصفات الإلهية بالتفصيل شارحاً ما يتعلق بكل منها مجيباً عن كل ما قد يرد عليها
ثم أتحدث عن النبوات : فأشرح معنى النبي والرسول ، وخصائص الأنبياء ، ولا بد من الإفاضة في البحث عند شرح ظاهرة الوحي وتحليلها ومعنى المعجزات وحقيقتها ، وموقف العقل والعلم من كل منهما .
فإذا انتقلت إلى البحث عن الكونيات ، تحدثت عن الإنسان والملائكة والجان وقانون السببية في الكون ، ولا بد من المقارنة عند ذلك بين حقيقة الإنسان وقصته كما يفصل القرآن فيها القول وكما ترى نظرية النشوء والتطور ، كما لا بد من التفصيل عند الحديث عن السببية والعلية في الكون تفصيلاً يجمع بين مقتضيات العلم وحاجة الإيضاح فإذا تحدثت عن الغيبيات ، بدأت بشرح معناها ، وذكرت القارئ بالمنهج العلمي للوصول إلى أمر يقيني بشأنها ، ثم أخذت أعددها الواحدة تلو الأخرى طبقاً للتسلسل الزمني ، أي بدءاً من أشراط الساعة ، فالموت ، فعذاب القبر ، فالحشر ، فالحساب فالميزان ، فالصراط ، فالجنة والنار ، راجياً أن يوفقني الله لحل كل مشكلة وردّ كل شبهة قد تعترض سبيل البحث العلمي في شيء من ذلك
And that I begin with the divine matters, so I present the scientific proof for the existence of the Creator, glorified be His Majesty, according to the clear methodology in the introduction starting from point zero in belief, in a style that combines convincing the ancient thinkers and the modern ones. Then I speak about the divine attributes in detail, explaining what pertains to each of them, answering everything that may be objected to them. Then I speak about prophethoods: so I explain the meaning of prophet and messenger, and the characteristics of the prophets, and it is necessary to elaborate in research when explaining the phenomenon of revelation and its analysis, and the meaning of miracles and their reality, and the stance of reason and science regarding each of them. Then when I move to the research about cosmic matters, I speak about humans, angels, jinn, and the law of causality in the universe, and it is necessary to compare at that point between the reality of humans and their story as the Qur'an details the statement therein and as the theory of evolution sees it, and it is also necessary to elaborate when speaking about causality and causation in the universe an elaboration that combines the requirements of science and the need for clarification. Then when I speak about the unseen matters, I begin by explaining their meaning, and I remind the reader of the scientific methodology to reach a certain matter regarding them, then I enumerate them one after another according to the chronological sequence, i.e., starting from the portents of the Hour, then death, then the torment of the grave, then the Resurrection, then the Reckoning, then the Scale, then the Path, then Paradise and Hell, hoping that Allah grants me success to solve every problem and refute every doubt that may obstruct the path of scientific research in any of that.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a methodological outline. The author states his plan to begin with the divine matters (ilahiyat), presenting a scientific proof for God's existence using a clear method starting from zero belief, appealing to both ancient and modern thinkers. Then he will detail the divine attributes. Next, he will address prophethoods (nubuwwat), explaining the meanings of prophet and messenger, their attributes, and analyzing revelation and miracles. Then he moves to cosmic matters (kawniyyat), discussing humans, angels, jinn, and causality, comparing the Qur'anic account with evolution. Finally, he will treat unseen matters (ghaybiyyat) chronologically: portents of the Hour, death, grave torment, Resurrection, Reckoning, Scale, Path, Paradise and Hell. He prays for success in solving problems and refuting doubts.

Method of Learning
beginner

Third Methodology: Certainties and the Impartial Intellect
Author commits to avoiding non-definitive proofs and concludes with a prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's methodological commitment to rely only on definitive proofs and his exhortation to approach theological inquiry with an impartial intellect and scientific balance.

Core Idea
Certainties require a unique methodology: start from nothing and follow impartial reason.

In this passage, the author crystallizes his approach to the study of creed: he will only employ proofs that are definitive and certain, avoiding elaboration on matters lacking solid evidence. He then transitions into a heartfelt prayer and exhortation, urging both himself and the reader to adopt a neutral starting point and follow the path of reason alone, free from bias and desire. This sets the tone for his entire work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the shift from methodological commitment to personal prayer.
The passage combines scholarly rigor with spiritual humility.
2
Identify the methodological commitment
Find the author's statement about not elaborating on matters without definitive proof. Understand why he restricts the book to certainties that are components of creed.
Key terms: دليل قطعي, برهان يقيني, مقومات العقيدة.
3
Reflect on the concluding prayer
Examine the prayer and exhortation. Note the emphasis on starting from 'the point of nothing', impartial reason, and avoiding partisanship. Consider the metaphor of life as a train speeding to death.
The prayer shows the author's reliance on God while advocating rational inquiry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : عدم الإطناب في ذكر الأمور التي لم يثبت فيها دليل قطعي وبرهان يقيني ، بل لعلي لن أتعرض لكثير منها . إذ المجال هنا مختص بتلك الأمور التي قامت على القطع واليقين ، فكانت بذلك من مقومات العقيدة التي لا يسع المسلم إنكارها أو تجاهلها . ومن المعلوم أن لليقينات منهجاً مختصاً بها لا ينبغي أن يستبدل به غيره في سبيل الوصول إليها هذا وأسأل الله تعالى أن يوفقني ويوفق القارئ لدى البدء في قراءة هذا الكتاب إلى أن لا نلتزم إلا جادة العقل المنصف الحر وحدها ، وأن نتخلص من كل عصبية وغرض وشهوة ، وأن نبدأ كما قلت آنفاً من نقطة اللاشيء ثم نسير خطوة فخطوة على ضوء الميزان العلمي النزيه ، فأي نهاية أوصلنا إليها هذا السبيل ، وقفنا عندها والتزمنا التمسك بها . وإنه الجدير بمن كانت حياته قطاراً يمر به دون هدوء إلى الموت ، أن يبحث في تلك النهاية الغامضة وما وراءها وما يتعلق بها بحثاً متجرداً لا يقوم إلا على هدى العقل وحده . فما رأيت أغرب من مظهر رجل يمتطي ركوباً يغذ به السير إلى حيث لا يعلم ، وهو مع جذلان لا يحاول أن يسأل نفسه ولو في لحظة واحدة عن النهاية التي سينتهي إليها وعما عساه يستطيع أن يفعله من أجل ذلك ذلك مرح وعلى كل فأنا أكتب هذه البحوث لا أبتغي بها إلا الكشف عن الحقيقة ، ولا أبتغي على ذلك إلا مثوبة من خالق هذه الحقيقة ومكوّنها . وللقارئ أن يبتغي بعد ذلك ما يشاء
Third: Not elaborating on matters for which there is no definitive proof and certain evidence; rather, perhaps I will not address many of them. For the field here is specific to those matters that are based on certainty and conviction, and thus they are among the components of creed that a Muslim cannot deny or ignore. And it is known that certainties have a methodology specific to them that should not be replaced by any other in the way of reaching them. This, and I ask Allah Almighty to grant me success and to grant the reader success upon beginning to read this book to adhere only to the path of the impartial, free intellect alone, and to rid ourselves of every partisanship, ulterior motive, and desire, and that we start, as I said earlier, from the point of nothing, then proceed step by step in the light of the impartial scientific balance. So whichever end this path leads us to, we stop at it and commit to holding fast to it. And it is worthy for one whose life is a train passing quickly towards death to investigate that mysterious end and what is beyond it and what pertains to it, with an impartial investigation based only on the guidance of the intellect alone. For I have not seen anything stranger than the sight of a man riding a mount that speeds onward to where he does not know, while he is cheerful, not trying to ask himself even for a moment about the end he will reach and what he might be able to do for that. That is heedlessness. And in any case, I write these researches seeking only to uncover the truth, and I seek thereby nothing but reward from the Creator of this truth and its Maker. And after that, the reader may seek whatever he wishes.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the third methodological commitment and a concluding exhortation. The author commits to avoiding elaboration on matters lacking definitive proof (dalil qat'i) and certain evidence (burhan yaqini). He restricts the book to certainties that constitute components of creed (muqawwimat al-'aqida) which a Muslim cannot deny. He notes that certainties have their own methodology that should not be substituted. Then he concludes with a prayer: he asks Allah to grant him and the reader success in adhering solely to the impartial free intellect, to abandon biases and desires, and to start from a neutral point (point of nothing) and proceed step by step with scientific balance. He emphasizes that one whose life is a train speeding to death should investigate the mysterious end and what lies beyond, using pure intellect. He criticizes those who ride heedlessly towards an unknown end without reflection. Finally, he declares his intention to seek only the truth and reward from God, and the reader may then seek what he wishes.

مقومات العقيدة

Misconception: Some may think the author rejects all theological reasoning or tradition.
Correction: The author is not rejecting all theological reasoning; he is insisting on using only certain evidence for creedal matters, and he combines this with prayer and reliance on God.

Key Takeaway

Al-Būṭī’s Method: Certainty and Rational Inquiry
Al-Būṭī states his method: focus only on certainties and follow unbiased reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Būṭī’s methodological principles: focusing on certainties, using impartial reason starting from a neutral point, and the purpose of seeking truth.

Core Idea
Certainties demand their own method: impartial reason starting from nothing.

Al-Būṭī opens his work by laying down his method. He will only discuss matters of certain proof, and he calls for a fresh, unbiased rational approach. This passage sets the tone for a rigorous, evidence-based theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong emphasis on certainty and reason.
2
Identify key methodological principles
What does al-Būṭī say about the scope of the book? What does he say about the method for certainties? How does he describe the role of intellect?
Look for three parts: limitation to certainty, method of certainty, and the call to impartial reason.
3
Reflect on the 'point of nothingness' metaphor
Al-Būṭī proposes starting from 'the point of nothingness.' What does this mean in practice? How does it relate to freeing oneself from partisanship? Consider the train metaphor as well.
This is a powerful call to intellectual humility and openness.

ثالثاً - عدم الإطناب في ذكر الأمور التي لم يثبت فيها دليل قطعي وبرهان يقيني ، بل لعلي لن أتعرض لكثير منها . إذ المجال هنا مختص بتلك الأمور التي قامت على القطع واليقين ، فكانت بذلك من مقومات العقيدة التي لا يسع المسلم إنكارها أو تجاهلها . ومن المعلوم أن لليقينات منهجاً مختصاً بها لا ينبغي أن يستبدل به غيره في سبيل الوصول إليها هذا وأسأل الله تعالى أن يوفقني ويوفق القارئ لدى البدء في قراءة هذا الكتاب إلى أن لا نلتزم إلا جادة العقل المنصف الحر وحدها ، وأن نتخلص من كل عصبية وغرض وشهوة ، وأن نبدأ كما قلت آنفاً من نقطة اللاشيء ثم نسير خطوة فخطوة على ضوء الميزان العلمي النزيه ، فأي نهاية أوصلنا إليها هذا السبيل ، وقفنا عندها والتزمنا التمسك بها . وإنه الجدير بمن كانت حياته قطاراً يمر به دون هدوء إلى الموت ، أن يبحث في تلك النهاية الغامضة وما وراءها وما يتعلق بها بحثاً متجرداً لا يقوم إلا على هدى العقل وحده . فما رأيت أغرب من مظهر رجل يمتطي ركوباً يغذ به السير إلى حيث لا يعلم ، وهو مع جذلان لا يحاول أن يسأل نفسه ولو في لحظة واحدة عن النهاية التي سينتهي إليها وعما عساه يستطيع أن يفعله من أجل ذلك . وعلى كل فأنا أكتب هذه البحوث لا أبتغي بها إلا الكشف عن الحقيقة ، ولا أبتغي على ذلك إلا مثوبة من خالق هذه الحقيقة ومكوّنها . وللقارئ أن يبتغي بعد ذلك ما يشاء . غرة شوال : ۱۳۸۸ هـ - TV- ۲۷ - الدكتور محمد سعيد رمضان البوطي
Third: Avoiding elaboration on matters for which there is no definitive proof (dalīl qaṭʿī) and certain demonstration (burhān yaqīnī). Rather, I will not even address many of them. For the field here is restricted to those matters that are based on certainty (qaṭʿ) and certitude (yaqīn), and thus become components of the creed (ʿaqīda) that a Muslim cannot deny or ignore. And it is known that certainties (yaqīniyyāt) have their own particular methodology that should not be replaced by another in seeking to attain them. This, and I ask Allah Almighty to grant me and the reader, upon beginning to read this book, that we adhere only to the path of the impartial free intellect (ʿaql munṣif ḥurr), and that we free ourselves from every partisanship (ʿaṣabiyya), ulterior motive (gharaḍ), and passion (shahwa). And that we begin, as I said earlier, from the point of nothingness (nuqṭat al-lāshayʾ), then proceed step by step in the light of the impartial scientific balance (mīzān ʿilmī nazīh). So whatever end this path leads us to, we stop at it and commit to holding firmly to it. And it is befitting for one whose life is a train passing through him without rest toward death, that he investigate that obscure end and what lies beyond it and what pertains to it, in an objectified research that stands only on the guidance of intellect (hudā al-ʿaql) alone. For I have seen nothing stranger than the sight of a man mounting a ride that speeds him along to where he knows not, while being joyful, not attempting to ask himself even for a moment about the end toward which he is heading and what he might be able to do about it. And in any case, I write these researches seeking only the disclosure of truth (al-ḥaqīqa), and I seek no reward for that except from the Creator of this truth and its Maker. After that, the reader may seek what he wishes. Beginning of Shawwal 1388 AH. - 27 - Dr. Muhammad Saʿīd Ramaḍān al-Būṭī.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is from the author's introduction, outlining his methodological approach in writing the book. He begins by stating his third point: he will avoid discussing matters that lack definitive proof and certain demonstration. He clarifies that his focus is only on those issues that are established with certainty, as they form the indispensable components of Islamic creed that a Muslim cannot deny. He then emphasizes that certainties have their own specific method, which must not be substituted. The author then turns to prayer: he asks Allah to guide both himself and the reader to follow only the path of the free and impartial intellect, free from partisanship, ulterior motives, and passion. He advocates starting from a neutral point—'the point of nothingness'—and proceeding step by step using the objective scientific scale. Whatever conclusion this method yields must be accepted and adhered to. He then uses a powerful metaphor: life is like a train speeding toward death; one should reflect on the unknown end and what lies beyond, engaging in dispassionate inquiry guided solely by reason. He criticizes those who travel joyfully toward an unknown destination without questioning their fate. Finally, he declares his sincerity: he writes solely to uncover truth, seeking reward only from the Creator. The reader is free to seek whatever they wish thereafter. This sets the tone for a rational, evidence-based approach to theology.

The Necessity of a Knowledge-Based Method
Buti establishes the epistemological principle that knowledge requires a knowledge-based method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a knowledge-based method is necessary for attaining certainty and why conjecture cannot produce knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge only comes from knowledge, never from guesswork.

This passage from Buti sets up a foundational rule for all seekers of truth: the method we use to find reality must itself be reliable. He explains that knowledge can only arise from knowledge, not from conjecture. Before we compare Islamic and Western approaches, we must grasp this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before you interpret it.
Note that the passage ends mid-sentence; we focus on the complete argument presented.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that knowledge is only generated from knowledge like it. Find where this is stated and notice the logical consequence: conjecture cannot lead to certainty.
Look for the phrase 'العلم لا يتولد إلا عن علم مثله'.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Why does the author say that two conjectural premises producing a certain result is an impossibility? Consider how this shapes the requirement for a scientific method.
This connects to the learning objective about method and certainty.

Firstly
From the appendix
According to Muslim scholars and others
If the perception of reality as it is in actuality is knowledge, as they say, then the method adopted for that perception must - without doubt - also be knowledge, meaning that the steps of this method in its reality should be nothing but a set of truthful perceptions that would unveil the truth being investigated.
That is because knowledge is only generated from knowledge like it, and conjecture cannot at all be a path to knowledge. Otherwise, two conjectural premises could produce a certain result, and that is among the clearest cases of impossibility.
Hence, every seeker of truth must lay out for it a scientific method unsullied by intuition or fancy, and must adhere to this method, not deviating from it right or left.
That is an evident truth, about which no one should dispute.
But it is very possible that we ask: To what extent did Islamic thought and Western thought become aware of this truth and care for it?
Perhaps the word 'objective research' - that widespread, common word which among some people has become known for its association with Orientalist research - hastened to answer this question.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction. The author begins by stating a foundational epistemological principle: knowledge is the perception of reality as it truly is. Given that goal, the method used to attain such knowledge must itself be knowledge-based. That is, every step of the method must consist of truthful perceptions that gradually unveil the truth. The reason is that knowledge can only arise from knowledge; conjecture can never produce certainty. If it could, then two conjectural premises could yield a certain conclusion, which the author declares an impossibility. Therefore, any researcher must adopt a strictly scientific method, free from intuition or illusion, and follow it without deviation. The author asserts this as an undeniable truth. Then he transitions to a comparison: to what extent did Islamic and Western thought recognize and heed this principle? He suggests that the term 'objective research' - often associated with Orientalist studies - might provide an answer, but the passage breaks off before completing the point.

الحدس
الوهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the author condemns all intuition, but he specifically rejects using intuition or fancy as a method for certainty, not intuition itself.
Correction: The passage states the method should be 'unsullied by intuition or fancy' (لا يشوبه الحدس أو الوهم), meaning that the method itself must be based on knowledge, not on subjective impressions. Intuition may have other uses, but it cannot be the foundation for a scientific method aimed at certainty.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge can only be built on knowledge; conjecture can never lead to certainty.
