Conditions of a Sound (Sahih) Report
The author defines the conditions for a saheeh report and describes the factors that make it unsound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exact conditions required for a report to be classified as sound (sahih) and what factors render it unsound.

Core Idea
A sound report requires a continuous chain of trustworthy narrators with no irregularity or defect.

Having established the three verifying sciences, the author now defines what makes a report 'sound' (sahih). He lists the precise conditions for soundness and the opposite conditions that make a report unsound. This lesson focuses on those criteria.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sahih definition
Read the Arabic passage that defines the first degree of soundness. Note the conditions mentioned.
The author uses 'أولى درجات الصحة' indicating there are higher levels.
2
Identify the conditions for soundness
List the four conditions: continuous chain, trustworthy narrators, no irregularity, no defect.
Each condition is necessary for sahih.
3
Understand what makes a report unsound
The author mentions several factors that cause a report to fall short of sahih. Identify them.
These include missing links, unknown narrators, lack of integrity or precision, and irregular text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السبيل المتخذة لتحقيق الخبر : تنهض بهذه السبيل فنون عديدة خاصة لم يعثر عليها التاريخ إلا في المكتبة الإسلامية . وهي : فن مصطلح الحديث ، وفن الجرح والتعديل وتراجم الرجال ، حيث تلتقي هذه الفنون الثلاثة على وضع ميزان دقيق يتضح فيه الخبر الصحيح من غيره والفرق بين الخبر الصحيح الذي يورث الظن والذي يورث اليقين الضابط عن فالخبر يرقى إلى أولى درجات ) الصحة ( عندما يثبت - لدى التحري والبحث - أن سلسلة السند متصلة من صاحب هذا الخبر ومصدره بنقل العدل مثله إلى نهايته التي انبثق منها دون أن يحتوي الخبر على شذوذ في جوهره أو علة في روايته . فإن تدانى الخبر عن هذه الرتبة ، بأن سقطت حلقة سلسلة الرواية بسبب الجهل به ، أو عدم الوثوق بعدالته ، أو عدم اليقين من بحفظه وضبطه ، أو بأن كان متن الخبر شاذاً بالنسبة للمقبول من غيره ، فهو غير صحيح ولكن الصحيح نفسه يرقى في درجات متفاوتة، تبدأ من الظن القوي إلى الإدراك اليقيني .. فإذا كانت السلسلة التي توفرت فيها مقومات الصحة مكونة من آحاد الرواة الذين ينتقل الخبر بينهم ، فهو لا يعدو أن يكون خبراً ظنياً في حكم العقل ، وإذا كانت حلقات السلسلة مكونة من راويين أو ثلاثة رواة ، فهو لا يزال خبراً ظنياً ، ولكنه ظن قوي يداني اليقين أما إذا غدت كل حلقة من الحلقات ، من الكثرة ، جموعاً يطمئن العقل إلى أنها لاتتواطأ على الكذب ، فإن الخبر المروي يكتسب عندئذ صفة اليقين ، وهو ما يسمى بالخبر المتواتر .
The means taken to verify the report: There rise to this means numerous specialized arts not found in history except in the Islamic library. They are: the art of hadith terminology, the art of jarh wa ta'dil (impugning and accrediting), and the art of biographies of men (tarajim al-rijal), where these three arts come together to set a precise scale by which the sound report is distinguished from others, and the difference between the sound report that yields probability (zann) and that which yields certainty (yaqin). The report ascends to the first degree of soundness when it is established – through investigation and research – that the chain of transmission is continuous from the owner of this report and its source, by the transmission of a trustworthy person like him, to its end from which it originated, without the report containing irregularity in its essence or a defect in its narration. If the report falls short of this rank, by a link of the chain of narration being missing due to ignorance of him, or lack of trust in his integrity, or lack of certainty in his memory and precision, or because the text of the report is irregular relative to what is accepted from others, then it is unsound. But the sound report itself ascends in varying degrees, starting from strong probability to certain perception. If the chain in which the elements of soundness are present consists of individual narrators among whom the report is transmitted, then it is nothing but a report of probability in the judgment of reason. If the links of the chain consist of two or three narrators, it is still a report of probability, but it is strong probability bordering on certainty. But if every link of the links becomes, due to multiplicity, masses that the mind is confident do not collude on falsehood, then the narrated report acquires at that time the quality of certainty, and that is what is called the mutawatir report.
Source pages p. 35

This passage defines the means of verifying reports and classifies the degrees of soundness. The author begins by identifying three specialized arts unique to the Islamic scholarly tradition: hadith terminology (mustalah al-hadith), criticism of narrators (jarh wa ta'dil), and biographical evaluation (tarajim al-rijal). These three together create a precise scale to distinguish sound reports from unsound, and to differentiate between reports that yield mere probability (zann) and those that yield certainty (yaqin). The author then defines the conditions for a report to be sound (sahih): a continuous chain of trustworthy narrators, no irregularity in the text, and no hidden defect. If any link is missing or the narrator is unknown, unreliable, or imprecise, or the text is irregular, the report is unsound. The author then explains that even sound reports vary in strength. Only when each link of the chain is composed of a large group that cannot plausibly collude on a lie does the report become certain (yaqini), which is called mutawatir. The author follows a clear logical progression, moving from the definition of the three sciences to the conditions of soundness, then to the gradations of sound reports from probable to certain.

From Probability to Certainty: The Grades of Khabar
The author grades sound reports from probable to certain and defines mutawatir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different degrees of sound reports—from probable knowledge (zann) to certainty (yaqin)—and the concept of tawatur.

Core Idea
Even sound reports vary in strength; only tawatur yields absolute certainty.

The author now explains that sound reports can still vary in their epistemic strength. He describes three categories: reports transmitted by a few individuals (khabar ahad) yield probability; those by two or three narrators yield strong probability near certainty; and when each link consists of a multitude that cannot plausibly conspire to lie, the report becomes certain (yaqin), known as mutawatir. This lesson examines these gradations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on degrees of soundness
Read the Arabic passage that describes the varying strengths of sound reports.
Notice the progression from zann to yaqin.
2
Identify the three levels
The author describes three scenarios based on the number of narrators per link. Find each one.
Level 1: ahad (individuals), Level 2: two or three, Level 3: multitudes.
3
Understand the epistemic value of each level
For each level, note whether it yields probability (zann) or certainty (yaqin).
Only the third level (tawatur) gives yaqin.

Speculative vs. Certain Reports in Creed and Practice
Author distinguishes speculative and certain reports in creed and practical rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why speculative sound reports are valid for practical rulings but not for creed, and why only certain (mutawatir) reports are binding in matters of belief.

Core Idea
Certainty is required for creed; probability suffices for practice.

This lesson begins by clarifying a foundational principle: not all sound hadiths carry the same weight. The Qur'an forbids following mere probability in matters of faith, but allows it in practical law. The author explains why speculative reports suffice for action but cannot compel belief, and why only mutawatir reports are authoritative for creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening distinction
Read the first part of the Arabic passage where the author distinguishes speculative (zanni) from certain (yaqini) reports. Notice the key terms: 'ظن' and 'يقين'.
2
Understand the ruling for speculative reports
The author states that speculative sound reports are not used for creed because the Quran prohibits following probability in belief. However, they are used for practical rulings.
The justification is that a mutawatir report and definitive proof obligate acting on speculative sound reports as a precaution.
3
Identify the role of certain reports
Only the certain (mutawatir) report is binding for creed. A person is not forced to believe based on a khabar ahad; any certainty from it is a matter of personal conviction.
This highlights the epistemological hierarchy: tawatur yields certainty, ahad yields probability.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
Consider how this principle affects daily Islamic practice: many fiqh rulings are based on ahad hadiths, and that is valid because the evidence for acting on them is decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الظني من الخبر الصحيح ، فلا يعتد به الحكم الإسلامي في بناء العقيدة لأنه إنما يفيد الظن ، ولقد نهى القرآن ) في مجال البحث في العقيدة ( عن اتباع الظن . كما قد رأيت . ولكن يعتد به في نطاق الأحكام العملية ، لثبوت الخبر المتواتر والدليل القطعي على أن المسلم مكلف - بالنسبة للسلوك العلمي - بالاعتماد على الظني من الخبر الصحيح ولذلك صح أن تستند الأحكام الشرعية إلى الأحاديث الصحيحة وإن كانت آحاداً ، وذلك حيطة في الأمر وأخذاً بالحزم . غير أن اليقيني من الخبر الصحيح ؛ وهو ما يسمى بالخبر المتواتر ، هو وحده الذي يعتد به في بناء العقيدة والمدركات اليقينية بمعنى أن الإنسان لا يجبر على الاعتقاد بشيء خبري إلا إذا كان قائماً على برهان التواتر . فإن كان دليلـه خبر آحاد ، كان اليقين به عائداً إلى القناعة الشخصية التي يراها من نفسه وتسالني : فمن أين للباحث أن يعلم شروط الخبر الصحيح ؟ ولنفرض أنـه سلسلة الرواية ، فكيف يستطيع أن يعلم اتصال هؤلاء الرواة ببعضهم ، وأنهم جميعاً ثقات عدول ضابطون سمع والجواب : أن كلاً من علمي : الجرح والتعديل، وتراجم الرجال ، إنما وجد تذليلاً لسبيل هذا البحث وتيسيراً للاطلاع على الواقع الذي ينبغي الوقوف عليه ففي مكتبتنا الإسلامية مؤلفات كثيرة تستعرض معجم الرجال الذين وردت أسماؤهم في أي سند من الأسانيد ، تستطيع أن تقف فيها على ترجمة من تشاء منهم جرحاً وتعديلاً ، وأن تضبط الزمن الذي عاش فيه ، لتعلم بذلك معاصريه الذين أمكنه أن يلتقي بهم . والغريب أن هؤلاء الأئمة الذين عكفوا على جمع تراجم الرجال - وهم أئمة ثقات يعتبر كل منهم مرجعاً في هذا الشأن ـ لم يبالوا ، في سبيل البحث عن الحقيقة واحترام الميزان العلمي أن لا يشوبه أي فساد ، أن يضعوا النقاط على حروفها في وصف الرجال وصفاً دقيقاً سواء انتهى إليهم بالجرح والتحذير منهم ، أم التعديل والتوثيق لهم
As for the speculative from the sound report, Islamic judgment does not rely on it in building creed, because it only benefits probability, and the Quran (in the field of research in creed) has prohibited following probability, as you have seen. But it is relied upon in the scope of practical rulings, due to the establishment of the mutawatir report and the definitive proof that the Muslim is obligated—with respect to practical conduct—to rely on the speculative from the sound report. Therefore it is correct that legal rulings are based on sound hadiths even if they are ahad (singular), as a precaution and taking the safe side. However, the certain from the sound report, which is called the mutawatir report, is the only one that is relied upon in building creed and certain perceptions, meaning that a person is not compelled to believe in a report-based matter unless it is based on the proof of tawatur. If its evidence is a khabar ahad (singular report), then certainty in it is due to personal conviction that he sees from himself. And you ask me: From where does the researcher know the conditions of the sound report? And suppose that the chain of narration is continuous, how can he know the connection of these narrators to each other, and that they are all trustworthy, upright, and precise? And the answer: that each of the two sciences: jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal, were only created to facilitate the path of this research and to make accessible the reality that should be known. In our Islamic library there are many works that survey the dictionary of men whose names appear in any chain, you can find in them the biography of whomever you wish, both impugning and accrediting, and you can determine the time in which he lived, to thereby know his contemporaries whom he could have met. And strange is that these imams who devoted themselves to collecting biographies of men—and they are trustworthy imams, each is considered a reference in this matter—did not care, in the path of seeking truth and respecting the scientific scale so that it be free from any corruption, to put the dots on the letters in describing the men precisely, whether it reached them by impugning and warning against them, or accrediting and declaring them reliable.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage begins by distinguishing the roles of speculative (zanni) and certain (yaqini) reports. The author states that speculative sound reports are not used in building creed (aqidah), because the Quran forbids following mere probability in matters of belief. However, they are valid for establishing practical legal rulings (ahkam amaliyya), because the mutawatir report and definitive proof establish that Muslims are obligated to act on speculative sound reports as a precaution. The author then emphasizes that only the certain mutawatir report is binding for creed; a person is not compelled to believe a report-based claim unless it is proven by tawatur. If the evidence is a khabar ahad, any certainty is due to personal conviction, not compulsion. The author then presents an objection: how can a researcher know the conditions of a sound report, such as the continuity of the chain and the reliability of narrators? The answer is that the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal were developed precisely to facilitate this research. The author describes the extensive biographical literature in the Islamic library, where one can find detailed evaluations of narrators, including their lifespan and contemporaries. The author notes the remarkable integrity of these imams: they did not hesitate to describe narrators honestly, whether impugning or accrediting them, in order to uphold truth and scientific rigor. The passage thus defends the epistemological framework of hadith criticism and its application to creed and practice.

يقين
عقيدة
حكم عملي

تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all sound hadiths are equally certain and equally valid for creed and practice.
Correction: The author clarifies that only mutawatir reports provide certainty for creed; ahad reports are sufficient for practice but not for belief.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say speculative sound reports are not used in building creed?
A) Because they are not actually sound
B) Because the Quran prohibits following probability in creed
C) Because they are only found in personal conviction
D) Because they are not mentioned in the Islamic library

Key Takeaway
Speculative sound reports are valid for practice but not creed; only mutawatir reports compel belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely accepted many religious beliefs from single hadiths or popular sermons. After this lesson, will you examine whether those beliefs are based on mutawātir reports or only on your personal conviction? What is one belief you might need to reconsider?
?
The author says you are not compelled to believe based on a khabar aḥad. Is there a belief you hold that you feel pressured by others to accept, but now realize you are not obligated to believe? How does that change your relationship with that belief?
?
In your daily practice, have you been acting on speculative hadiths with the same sense of duty as on certain ones? How does the principle of 'precaution' (al-ḥazm) in this lesson affect your commitment to following such hadiths? Are you willing to act on them even without certainty?

How to Verify the Soundness of Reports: Objection and Answer
Author answers an objection about verifying sound reports using jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars of jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal enable researchers to verify the conditions of sound reports, such as continuity of chain and reliability of narrators.

Core Idea
Verification of reports is possible through systematic biographical criticism.

A natural question arises: how can a researcher know the conditions of a sound report, like the continuity of narrators and their reliability? The author answers by pointing to the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil (impugnment and accreditation) and tarajim al-rijal (biographies of narrators). He describes the rich biographical literature and the remarkable integrity of the scholars who compiled them.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection posed by the author
Read the part where the author presents the objection: 'From where does the researcher know the conditions of the sound report...?' This is a challenge to the system.
2
Understand the answer: jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal
The author states that these two sciences were created precisely to facilitate research into chains and narrators. They provide detailed information about each narrator's reliability.
Jarh wa ta'dil evaluates credibility; tarajim al-rijal provides biographies.
3
Learn about the biographical literature
The author mentions the vast Islamic library of biographical works where one can find entries on any narrator, including their lifespan, teachers, and students.
4
Appreciate the integrity of the scholars
The author notes that these imams did not hesitate to describe narrators honestly, whether criticizing or praising, in order to uphold truth and scientific rigor.
This demonstrates the objectivity of hadith criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الظني من الخبر الصحيح ، فلا يعتد به الحكم الإسلامي في بناء العقيدة لأنه إنما يفيد الظن ، ولقد نهى القرآن ) في مجال البحث في العقيدة ( عن اتباع الظن . كما قد رأيت . ولكن يعتد به في نطاق الأحكام العملية ، لثبوت الخبر المتواتر والدليل القطعي على أن المسلم مكلف - بالنسبة للسلوك العلمي - بالاعتماد على الظني من الخبر الصحيح ولذلك صح أن تستند الأحكام الشرعية إلى الأحاديث الصحيحة وإن كانت آحاداً ، وذلك حيطة في الأمر وأخذاً بالحزم . غير أن اليقيني من الخبر الصحيح ؛ وهو ما يسمى بالخبر المتواتر ، هو وحده الذي يعتد به في بناء العقيدة والمدركات اليقينية بمعنى أن الإنسان لا يجبر على الاعتقاد بشيء خبري إلا إذا كان قائماً على برهان التواتر . فإن كان دليلـه خبر آحاد ، كان اليقين به عائداً إلى القناعة الشخصية التي يراها من نفسه وتسالني : فمن أين للباحث أن يعلم شروط الخبر الصحيح ؟ ولنفرض أنـه سلسلة الرواية ، فكيف يستطيع أن يعلم اتصال هؤلاء الرواة ببعضهم ، وأنهم جميعاً ثقات عدول ضابطون سمع والجواب : أن كلاً من علمي : الجرح والتعديل، وتراجم الرجال ، إنما وجد تذليلاً لسبيل هذا البحث وتيسيراً للاطلاع على الواقع الذي ينبغي الوقوف عليه ففي مكتبتنا الإسلامية مؤلفات كثيرة تستعرض معجم الرجال الذين وردت أسماؤهم في أي سند من الأسانيد ، تستطيع أن تقف فيها على ترجمة من تشاء منهم جرحاً وتعديلاً ، وأن تضبط الزمن الذي عاش فيه ، لتعلم بذلك معاصريه الذين أمكنه أن يلتقي بهم . والغريب أن هؤلاء الأئمة الذين عكفوا على جمع تراجم الرجال - وهم أئمة ثقات يعتبر كل منهم مرجعاً في هذا الشأن ـ لم يبالوا ، في سبيل البحث عن الحقيقة واحترام الميزان العلمي أن لا يشوبه أي فساد ، أن يضعوا النقاط على حروفها في وصف الرجال وصفاً دقيقاً سواء انتهى إليهم بالجرح والتحذير منهم ، أم التعديل والتوثيق لهم
As for the speculative from the sound report, Islamic judgment does not rely on it in building creed, because it only benefits probability, and the Quran (in the field of research in creed) has prohibited following probability, as you have seen. But it is relied upon in the scope of practical rulings, due to the establishment of the mutawatir report and the definitive proof that the Muslim is obligated—with respect to practical conduct—to rely on the speculative from the sound report. Therefore it is correct that legal rulings are based on sound hadiths even if they are ahad (singular), as a precaution and taking the safe side. However, the certain from the sound report, which is called the mutawatir report, is the only one that is relied upon in building creed and certain perceptions, meaning that a person is not compelled to believe in a report-based matter unless it is based on the proof of tawatur. If its evidence is a khabar ahad (singular report), then certainty in it is due to personal conviction that he sees from himself. And you ask me: From where does the researcher know the conditions of the sound report? And suppose that the chain of narration is continuous, how can he know the connection of these narrators to each other, and that they are all trustworthy, upright, and precise? And the answer: that each of the two sciences: jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal, were only created to facilitate the path of this research and to make accessible the reality that should be known. In our Islamic library there are many works that survey the dictionary of men whose names appear in any chain, you can find in them the biography of whomever you wish, both impugning and accrediting, and you can determine the time in which he lived, to thereby know his contemporaries whom he could have met. And strange is that these imams who devoted themselves to collecting biographies of men—and they are trustworthy imams, each is considered a reference in this matter—did not care, in the path of seeking truth and respecting the scientific scale so that it be free from any corruption, to put the dots on the letters in describing the men precisely, whether it reached them by impugning and warning against them, or accrediting and declaring them reliable.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage begins by distinguishing the roles of speculative (zanni) and certain (yaqini) reports. The author states that speculative sound reports are not used in building creed (aqidah), because the Quran forbids following mere probability in matters of belief. However, they are valid for establishing practical legal rulings (ahkam amaliyya), because the mutawatir report and definitive proof establish that Muslims are obligated to act on speculative sound reports as a precaution. The author then emphasizes that only the certain mutawatir report is binding for creed; a person is not compelled to believe a report-based claim unless it is proven by tawatur. If the evidence is a khabar ahad, any certainty is due to personal conviction, not compulsion. The author then presents an objection: how can a researcher know the conditions of a sound report, such as the continuity of the chain and the reliability of narrators? The answer is that the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal were developed precisely to facilitate this research. The author describes the extensive biographical literature in the Islamic library, where one can find detailed evaluations of narrators, including their lifespan and contemporaries. The author notes the remarkable integrity of these imams: they did not hesitate to describe narrators honestly, whether impugning or accrediting them, in order to uphold truth and scientific rigor. The passage thus defends the epistemological framework of hadith criticism and its application to creed and practice.

تراجم الرجال
سند
ثقات
عدول
ضابطون

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is impossible to know the reliability of narrators because they lived long ago.
Correction: The author shows that systematic biographical criticism provides detailed information about narrators, enabling verification.

B) The sciences of jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal
C) The number of hadiths in a collection
D) The length of the chain

Key Takeaway
Jarh wa ta'dil and tarajim al-rijal provide the tools to verify the soundness of reports and their narrators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The imams who compiled biographical works 'did not care, in the path of seeking truth and respecting the scientific scale, to put the dots on the letters in describing the men precisely.' In your own life, when you speak about others, are you equally committed to accuracy and fairness? Can you recall a recent situation where you were careless with words about someone? What would it cost you to correct that?
?
These scholars created systematic tools to verify every report they received. Think about the information you consume daily about your faith, your community, or even your own self—how much of it do you verify before acting? What would change in your deen if you applied a fraction of their rigorous method to the 'hadith' you hear on social media?
?
The passage says the sciences were created 'to make accessible the reality that should be known.' Are you actively seeking that reality, or are you content with surface-level knowledge? Zann and Yaqin: The Twofold Role of Reports
Buti states the principle that zanni reports are used in practice but not creed, citing Quranic prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why speculative (zanni) reports are accepted in practical rulings but not in creed.

Core Idea
Zann guides action, yaqin guides belief.

Buti begins by clarifying a foundational epistemological distinction: reports that yield only probability (zann) are sufficient for practical guidance, but the Quran forbids following zann in matters of creed. This lesson unpacks that principle and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic prohibition
Read the first part of the passage where Buti states that the Quran forbids following zann in creed. Note the phrase 'في مجال البحث في العقيدة'.
This is the starting point for the whole discussion.
2
Understand the exception for practice
Notice that Buti immediately says zann is taken into account for practical rulings. Look for the reason he gives: the mutawatir report and definitive proof that Muslims must rely on authentic zanni reports in practice.
The word 'ولكن' signals the turn.
3
See the application to hadith
Buti concludes that legal rulings can be based on authentic ahad hadiths, as a precaution (حيطة). Ask yourself why this is permissible despite the Quranic prohibition on following zann in creed.
This shows the practical wisdom in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنه إنما يفيد الظن ، ولقد نهى القرآن ) في مجال البحث في العقيدة ( عن اتباع الظن . كما قد رأيت . ولكن يعتد به في نطاق الأحكام العملية ، لثبوت الخبر المتواتر والدليل القطعي على أن المسلم مكلف - بالنسبة للسلوك العلمي - بالاعتماد على الظني من الخبر الصحيح ولذلك صح أن تستند الأحكام الشرعية إلى الأحاديث الصحيحة وإن كانت آحاداً ، وذلك حيطة في الأمر وأخذاً بالحزم . غير أن اليقيني من الخبر الصحيح ؛ وهو ما يسمى بالخبر المتواتر ، هو وحده الذي يعتد به في بناء العقيدة والمدركات اليقينية بمعنى أن الإنسان لا يجبر على الاعتقاد بشيء خبري إلا إذا كان قائماً على برهان التواتر . فإن كان دليلـه خبر آحاد ، كان اليقين به عائداً إلى القناعة الشخصية التي يراها من نفسه وتسألني : فمن أين للباحث أن يعلم شروط الخبر الصحيح ؟ ولنفرض أنـه سلسلة الرواية ، فكيف يستطيع أن يعلم اتصال هؤلاء الرواة ببعضهم ، وأنهم جميعاً ثقات عدول ضابطون سمع والجواب : أن كلاً من علمي : الجرح والتعديل، وتراجم الرجال ، إنما وجد تذليلاً لسبيل هذا البحث وتيسيراً للاطلاع على الواقع الذي ينبغي الوقوف عليه ففي مكتبتنا الإسلامية مؤلفات كثيرة تستعرض معجم الرجال الذين وردت أسماؤهم في أي سند من الأسانيد ، تستطيع أن تقف فيها على ترجمة من تشاء منهم جرحاً وتعديلاً ، وأن تضبط الزمن الذي عاش فيه ، لتعلم بذلك معاصريه الذين أمكنه أن يلتقي بهم . والغريب أن هؤلاء الأئمة الذين عكفوا على جمع تراجم الرجال - وهم أئمة ثقات يعتبر كل منهم مرجعاً في هذا الشأن ـ لم يبالوا ، في سبيل البحث عن الحقيقة واحترام الميزان العلمي أن لا يشوبه أي فساد ، أن يضعوا النقاط على حروفها في وصف الرجال وصفاً دقيقاً سواء انتهى إليهم بالجرح والتحذير منهم ، أم التعديل والتوثيق لهم مختلف وهكذا ، فقد تكونت في مكتبتنا الإسلامية ، قواميس من نوع قواميس لضبط الأشخاص والرجال ، تقف منها على الزيف والدخيل الضعيف ، بالسهولة ذاتها التي تقف بها على ضبط الكلمة وتقويمها في قواميس اللغة ومعاجمها المعروفة كما قد تكوّن في مكتبتنا فن خاص بهذا الشأن ، وهو ما يسمى بفن مصطلح الحديث ، وقد ضم هذا الفن كل المقومات المختلفة للتحقيق في النقل والأخبار طبق منهج علمي فريد . تلك خلاصة سريعة عن السبيل العلمي لدى علماء الإسلام لتحقيق النقل والخبر ، ولا مطمع في هذه الكلمة السريعة بمزيد من الشرح والتفصيل ، ولكن على من يرغب في الاستزادة أن يعكف على الفنون التي ألمعنا إليها ليجد الجهد الغريب المعجز في سبيل استخراج القيمة العلمية من « الكلمة » المنقولة
Because it only yields opinion (zann), and the Qur'an has forbidden following opinion in the field of researching creed, as you have seen. But it is taken into account in the scope of practical rulings, due to the established mutawatir report and the definitive proof that the Muslim is obligated—with respect to practical conduct—to rely on the speculative (zanni) from the authentic report. Therefore, it is correct that legal rulings are based on authentic hadiths even if they are solitary (ahad), as a precaution and taking the safer course. However, the certain (yaqini) from the authentic report—which is called the mutawatir report—alone is relied upon in building creed and certain perceptions. That is, a person is not compelled to believe in a transmitted thing unless it is based on the proof of tawatur. If its evidence is a solitary report (khabar ahad), then certainty about it depends on personal conviction that one sees in himself. And you ask: From where does the researcher know the conditions of the authentic report? And suppose it is a chain of transmission, how can he know the connection of these narrators to each other, and that they are all trustworthy, upright, and precise? The answer: Each of the two sciences: jarh wa ta'dil (impugnment and validation) and biographical dictionaries (tarajim al-rijal) came into existence to facilitate this research and to make possible access to the reality that should be known. In our Islamic library there are many works that review the dictionary of men whose names appear in any chain of transmission; you can find in them the biography of whomever you wish, both in terms of impugnment and validation, and you can determine the time in which he lived, thereby knowing his contemporaries whom he could have met. Remarkably, these imams who devoted themselves to collecting biographies of men—and they are trustworthy imams, each considered a reference in this matter—did not hesitate, in pursuit of truth and respect for scientific standards so that no corruption may taint them, to put the dots on the letters in describing the men precisely, whether it came to them as impugnment and warning against them, or validation and authentication of them. And thus, dictionaries of the kind for recording persons and men have been formed in our Islamic library, by which you can identify falsehood and weak, spurious elements with the same ease with which you identify correct pronunciation and rectification in known dictionaries and lexicons of the language. Also, a specific art has been formed in our library concerning this matter, which is called the art of mustalah al-hadith (terminology of hadith), and this art encompasses all the various components for investigating transmission and reports according to a unique scientific methodology. That is a brief summary of the scientific method among Islamic scholars for verifying transmission and reports. There is no aspiration in this brief word for more explanation and detail, but whoever wishes for more should devote himself to the arts we have indicated to find the wondrous and extraordinary effort in extracting the scientific value from the transmitted word.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage explains the distinction between speculative (zanni) and certain (yaqini) reports in Islamic epistemology, particularly their application to creed versus practical law. The author begins by noting that speculative reports are only useful for practical rulings due to the presence of mutawatir evidence requiring reliance on authentic zanni reports, but certainty in creed demands mutawatir reports. He then answers how one can verify the reliability of narrators: through the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil and biographical dictionaries, which are comprehensive and precise. Finally, he highlights the unique art of mustalah al-hadith as a culmination of this methodology.

خبر آحاد

Key Takeaway

Mutawatir: The Only Basis for Certainty in Creed
Buti states that only mutawatir reports are binding in creed; ahad reports produce only personal conviction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why only mutawatir reports compel belief in creed, while ahad reports only give personal conviction.

Core Idea
Certainty in creed requires tawatur.

Having established that zanni reports are used in practice, Buti now turns to the higher standard for creed. He declares that the certain (yaqini) report, the mutawatir, is the only basis for obligatory belief in matters of faith. This lesson examines that ruling and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the ruling on mutawatir
Read the sentence beginning with 'غير أن اليقيني'. Note that Buti identifies the certain report as the mutawatir, and says it alone is relied upon for building creed.
The word 'وحده' emphasizes exclusivity.
2
Understand the consequence for ahad reports
Read the next sentence about ahad reports. Buti says that if the evidence is a khabar ahad, certainty becomes a matter of personal conviction, not obligation.
This distinguishes between personal certainty and creedal obligation.
3
Reflect on the practical implication
Ask yourself: How does this affect what Muslims must believe? Only mutawatir reports can be made obligatory in matters of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنه إنما يفيد الظن ، ولقد نهى القرآن ) في مجال البحث في العقيدة ( عن اتباع الظن . كما قد رأيت . ولكن يعتد به في نطاق الأحكام العملية ، لثبوت الخبر المتواتر والدليل القطعي على أن المسلم مكلف - بالنسبة للسلوك العلمي - بالاعتماد على الظني من الخبر الصحيح ولذلك صح أن تستند الأحكام الشرعية إلى الأحاديث الصحيحة وإن كانت آحاداً ، وذلك حيطة في الأمر وأخذاً بالحزم . غير أن اليقيني من الخبر الصحيح ؛ وهو ما يسمى بالخبر المتواتر ، هو وحده الذي يعتد به في بناء العقيدة والمدركات اليقينية بمعنى أن الإنسان لا يجبر على الاعتقاد بشيء خبري إلا إذا كان قائماً على برهان التواتر . فإن كان دليلـه خبر آحاد ، كان اليقين به عائداً إلى القناعة الشخصية التي يراها من نفسه وتسألني : فمن أين للباحث أن يعلم شروط الخبر الصحيح ؟ ولنفرض أنـه سلسلة الرواية ، فكيف يستطيع أن يعلم اتصال هؤلاء الرواة ببعضهم ، وأنهم جميعاً ثقات عدول ضابطون سمع والجواب : أن كلاً من علمي : الجرح والتعديل، وتراجم الرجال ، إنما وجد تذليلاً لسبيل هذا البحث وتيسيراً للاطلاع على الواقع الذي ينبغي الوقوف عليه ففي مكتبتنا الإسلامية مؤلفات كثيرة تستعرض معجم الرجال الذين وردت أسماؤهم في أي سند من الأسانيد ، تستطيع أن تقف فيها على ترجمة من تشاء منهم جرحاً وتعديلاً ، وأن تضبط الزمن الذي عاش فيه ، لتعلم بذلك معاصريه الذين أمكنه أن يلتقي بهم . والغريب أن هؤلاء الأئمة الذين عكفوا على جمع تراجم الرجال - وهم أئمة ثقات يعتبر كل منهم مرجعاً في هذا الشأن ـ لم يبالوا ، في سبيل البحث عن الحقيقة واحترام الميزان العلمي أن لا يشوبه أي فساد ، أن يضعوا النقاط على حروفها في وصف الرجال وصفاً دقيقاً سواء انتهى إليهم بالجرح والتحذير منهم ، أم التعديل والتوثيق لهم مختلف وهكذا ، فقد تكونت في مكتبتنا الإسلامية ، قواميس من نوع قواميس لضبط الأشخاص والرجال ، تقف منها على الزيف والدخيل الضعيف ، بالسهولة ذاتها التي تقف بها على ضبط الكلمة وتقويمها في قواميس اللغة ومعاجمها المعروفة كما قد تكوّن في مكتبتنا فن خاص بهذا الشأن ، وهو ما يسمى بفن مصطلح الحديث ، وقد ضم هذا الفن كل المقومات المختلفة للتحقيق في النقل والأخبار طبق منهج علمي فريد . تلك خلاصة سريعة عن السبيل العلمي لدى علماء الإسلام لتحقيق النقل والخبر ، ولا مطمع في هذه الكلمة السريعة بمزيد من الشرح والتفصيل ، ولكن على من يرغب في الاستزادة أن يعكف على الفنون التي ألمعنا إليها ليجد الجهد الغريب المعجز في سبيل استخراج القيمة العلمية من « الكلمة » المنقولة
Because it only yields opinion (zann), and the Qur'an has forbidden following opinion in the field of researching creed, as you have seen. But it is taken into account in the scope of practical rulings, due to the established mutawatir report and the definitive proof that the Muslim is obligated—with respect to practical conduct—to rely on the speculative (zanni) from the authentic report. Therefore, it is correct that legal rulings are based on authentic hadiths even if they are solitary (ahad), as a precaution and taking the safer course. However, the certain (yaqini) from the authentic report—which is called the mutawatir report—alone is relied upon in building creed and certain perceptions. That is, a person is not compelled to believe in a transmitted thing unless it is based on the proof of tawatur. If its evidence is a solitary report (khabar ahad), then certainty about it depends on personal conviction that one sees in himself. And you ask: From where does the researcher know the conditions of the authentic report? And suppose it is a chain of transmission, how can he know the connection of these narrators to each other, and that they are all trustworthy, upright, and precise? The answer: Each of the two sciences: jarh wa ta'dil (impugnment and validation) and biographical dictionaries (tarajim al-rijal) came into existence to facilitate this research and to make possible access to the reality that should be known. In our Islamic library there are many works that review the dictionary of men whose names appear in any chain of transmission; you can find in them the biography of whomever you wish, both in terms of impugnment and validation, and you can determine the time in which he lived, thereby knowing his contemporaries whom he could have met. Remarkably, these imams who devoted themselves to collecting biographies of men—and they are trustworthy imams, each considered a reference in this matter—did not hesitate, in pursuit of truth and respect for scientific standards so that no corruption may taint them, to put the dots on the letters in describing the men precisely, whether it came to them as impugnment and warning against them, or validation and authentication of them. And thus, dictionaries of the kind for recording persons and men have been formed in our Islamic library, by which you can identify falsehood and weak, spurious elements with the same ease with which you identify correct pronunciation and rectification in known dictionaries and lexicons of the language. Also, a specific art has been formed in our library concerning this matter, which is called the art of mustalah al-hadith (terminology of hadith), and this art encompasses all the various components for investigating transmission and reports according to a unique scientific methodology. That is a brief summary of the scientific method among Islamic scholars for verifying transmission and reports. There is no aspiration in this brief word for more explanation and detail, but whoever wishes for more should devote himself to the arts we have indicated to find the wondrous and extraordinary effort in extracting the scientific value from the transmitted word.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage explains the distinction between speculative (zanni) and certain (yaqini) reports in Islamic epistemology, particularly their application to creed versus practical law. The author begins by noting that speculative reports are only useful for practical rulings due to the presence of mutawatir evidence requiring reliance on authentic zanni reports, but certainty in creed demands mutawatir reports. He then answers how one can verify the reliability of narrators: through the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil and biographical dictionaries, which are comprehensive and precise. Finally, he highlights the unique art of mustalah al-hadith as a culmination of this methodology.

Key Terms
يقين
خبر متواتر
خبر آحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that any authentic ahad hadith can establish obligatory belief in creed.
Correction: Buti clearly states that only mutawatir reports compel belief; ahad reports only give personal conviction.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the basis for obligatory certainty in matters of creed concerning transmitted reports?
A) The authenticity of the report (sihha)
B) The report being mutawatir
C) The report being ahad
D) Personal conviction

Key Takeaway
Only mutawatir reports obligate belief in creed; ahad reports yield only personal certainty.

The Sciences of Hadith Verification
Buti describes the tools for verifying transmissions: jarh wa ta'dil, biographical dictionaries, and mustalah al-hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic scholars developed sciences like jarh wa ta'dil and mustalah al-hadith to verify the authenticity of transmitted reports.

Core Idea
Hadith verification is a rigorous scientific discipline.

Buti now answers the practical question: How can a researcher know the conditions of an authentic report? He points to the sophisticated scholarly apparatus developed by Muslim scholars—biographical dictionaries, the science of jarh wa ta'dil, and the art of mustalah al-hadith. This lesson explores that unique methodology and its tools.

Guided Path
1
Read the question posed by the hypothetical asker
Find the sentence starting with 'وتسألني'. Buti sets up a question: how does a researcher know the conditions of a sound report, especially the chain of narrators?
This question drives the rest of the passage.
2
Identify the two sciences mentioned
In the answer, Buti names 'الجرح والتعديل' and 'تراجم الرجال'. These are the sciences that facilitate verification.
Each serves a distinct purpose: jarh critiques narrators, ta'dil validates them; biographical dictionaries provide context.
3
Note the comprehensiveness of the dictionaries
Read how Buti describes the dictionaries: they allow one to find a narrator's biography, including his trustworthiness and time period, to verify connections.
This demonstrates the systematic nature of the methodology.
4
Understand the unique art of mustalah al-hadith
Finally, Buti mentions the art of hadith terminology as a distinct field that integrates all components of investigation.
He calls it a 'unique scientific methodology'.

?
When you hear a hadith, do you ever pause to ask how it was verified, or do you uncritically accept it if it sounds good? This lesson shows the immense effort behind authentic transmission. What is one thing you will do this week to verify a hadith before sharing it with others?
?
The imams sacrificed their comfort to compile biographical dictionaries in pursuit of truth. Are you willing to invest similar effort to ensure the knowledge you rely on is sound—whether in religion or in daily life? What step can you take today to be more rigorous in checking your sources?
?
You are responsible for what you believe and teach about Allah and His Messenger. If you discover that a belief you hold is based on weak evidence, are you ready to abandon it? This lesson reveals the tools available. What will you do to examine your own convictions in light of this scientific method?

Islam and Empirical Science: Buti's Method
Buti outlines the method of verification for material claims via senses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's argument that Islam accepts empirical evidence for material claims and that no scientific truth contradicts Islamic creed.

Core Idea
Islam embraces empirical science; no scientific fact contradicts the creed.

Buti here addresses a pivotal question: how do we verify claims about physical objects? He argues that sensory observation is the only valid method, and that Islam fully endorses this. He also highlights the harmony between scientific findings and Islamic beliefs, noting that the Quran and Sunnah do not provide specific material information but encourage reflection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without focusing on details. Then read the translation to understand the flow.
Notice that Buti starts by stating the method differs by claim type.
2
Identify Buti's main points
Identify two key claims: (1) Material claims require sensory evidence. (2) Islam adopts whatever is proven by this means, and no scientific truth contradicts the creed.
3
Reflect on Islam and science
Consider how Buti positions Islam as supportive of empirical investigation. Note his statement about Quran/Sunnah not burdening us with specific material info.
This relates to the common misunderstanding that Islam opposes science.
4
Take the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to check your understanding of Islam's stance on empirical knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السبيل المتخذة للتحقيق في الادعاء : يختلف هذا السبيل كما قلنا ، حسب اختلاف نوع الادعاء . فما كان منه متعلقاً بموجود مادي يتناوله تحليلاً أو تكييفاً ، فلا بد من الاعتماد فيه على شواهد وبراهين من الحواس الخمس ، أي على ما يسمى بالتعبير الحديث ( التجربة والمشاهدة ) . إذ هي الوسيلة الطبيعية إلى الإدراك اليقيني في مثل هذه الأمور.والإسلام لا يتردد في تبني كل ما يثبت تحقيقاً بهذه الوسيلة أما من الناحية العكسية ، فإن العلم لم يستطع أن يقدم لنا إلى اليوم أي حقيقة علمية تخالف أي جزئية من جزئيات العقيدة الإسلامية ولم يكلفنا شيء من الكتاب والسنة بأي معلومات خاصة صريحة تتعلق بالموجودات المادية القائمة من حولنا ، اللهم إلا ما أشار إليه منها في عبارات تحمل على الفكر والتأمل فيها أكثر من أن تبلغنا أي معلومات عنها ، وذلك
The method taken for verification of a claim: This method differs, as we said, according to the type of claim. Whatever relates to a material object that can be analyzed or classified, it is necessary to rely on evidence and proofs from the five senses, i.e., on what is called in modern expression (experiment and observation). For it is the natural means to certain perception in such matters. And Islam does not hesitate to adopt everything that is proven authentically by this means. As for the opposite side, science has not been able to present to us up to today any scientific truth that contradicts any particular of the Islamic creed. And nothing from the Book or the Sunnah has burdened us with any specific explicit information concerning the material objects around us, except what is indicated in them in expressions that encourage thought and reflection upon them more than they convey any information about them, and that...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains the method for verifying claims about material objects: reliance on sensory evidence, experiment, and observation. The author asserts that this is the natural path to certain knowledge in such matters, and that Islam fully accepts whatever is proven by this method. He also points out that no scientific truth has ever contradicted Islamic creed, and that the Quran and Sunnah do not provide specific information about material objects but rather encourage reflection.

Key Terms
حواس خمس
تجربة ومشاهدة
إدراك يقيني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Islam is opposed to empirical science and rejects sensory evidence.
Correction: Buti asserts that Islam adopts everything proven authentically by sensory evidence, and no scientific truth contradicts Islamic creed.

Checkpoint
What does Buti say about Islam's stance on empirical knowledge?
A) Islam rejects empirical knowledge
B) Islam adopts whatever is proven by sensory evidence
C) Islam only accepts revelation
D) Islam considers empirical knowledge as zanni

Key Takeaway
Islam endorses empirical science for material claims, and no scientific fact contradicts the Islamic creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a scientific claim that seems to clash with your faith, do you instinctively reject it or pause to verify its authenticity? Buti states that no real scientific fact contradicts the creed. How would remembering this change your response the next time you face such a conflict? What action will you take to ensure you don't prematurely dismiss genuine knowledge?
?
Buti asserts that the Quran and Sunnah do not provide scientific specifics but rather encourage reflection. Have you ever forced a verse to support a scientific theory you believed in? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's wisdom versus your need for validation from modern science? Will you commit to reading such verses purely for guidance and reflection from now on?
?
In your daily life, which source do you rely on more for decisions about material matters—your senses and empirical data, or your religious texts? Buti affirms that both are valid in their own domains. Are there areas where you ignore empirical evidence because of a false piety, or areas where you neglect revelation entirely? How will you balance the two starting today?

Biographical Dictionaries and Hadith Terminology as Verification Tools
Buti summarizes the Islamic method for verifying reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Muslim scholars developed specialized biographical dictionaries and hadith terminology to verify transmitted reports.

Core Idea
Islamic scholarship created tools to verify reports with the same precision as correcting a word in a dictionary.

Buti presents a concise summary of the rigorous methodology that Muslim scholars developed for verifying transmitted reports. He draws a parallel between correcting words in a language dictionary and detecting falsehoods in reports through biographical dictionaries. This lesson introduces the twin pillars of this verification system: the biographical dictionaries and the discipline of hadith terminology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own summary come through before you interpret.
Notice the parallel between language dictionaries and biographical dictionaries.
2
Identify the two main tools
The passage mentions two kinds of tools formed in the Islamic library. Find them and note how they relate to verifying reports.
3
Reflect on the scientific methodology
Consider why the author describes this as a 'unique scientific methodology.' Think about how these tools work together to extract scientific value from transmitted words.

مختلف وهكذا ، فقد تكونت في مكتبتنا الإسلامية ، قواميس من نوع قواميس لضبط الأشخاص والرجال ، تقف منها على الزيف والدخيل الضعيف ، بالسهولة ذاتها التي تقف بها على ضبط الكلمة وتقويمها في قواميس اللغة ومعاجمها المعروفة كما قد تكوّن في مكتبتنا فن خاص بهذا الشأن ، وهو ما يسمى بفن مصطلح الحديث ، وقد ضم هذا الفن كل المقومات المختلفة للتحقيق في النقل والأخبار طبق منهج علمي فريد . تلك خلاصة سريعة عن السبيل العلمي لدى علماء الإسلام لتحقيق النقل والخبر ، ولا مطمع في هذه الكلمة السريعة بمزيد من الشرح والتفصيل ، ولكن على من يرغب في الاستزادة أن يعكف على الفنون التي ألمعنا إليها ليجد الجهد الغريب المعجز في سبيل استخراج القيمة العلمية من « الكلمة » المنقولة
Various and so forth. Thus, there were formed in our Islamic library dictionaries of the type of dictionaries for controlling persons and men, by which you can detect falsehood and weak interpolation with the same ease that you can control a word and correct it in the well-known language dictionaries and lexicons. Also, there was formed in our library a specific art concerning this matter, which is called the art of hadith terminology (mustalah al-hadith). This art has included all the various components for investigating transmission and reports according to a unique scientific methodology. That is a brief summary of the scientific method of Muslim scholars for verifying transmission and reports. There is no aspiration in this brief statement for more explanation and detail, but whoever desires further study should devote himself to the arts we have alluded to, to find the astonishing and miraculous effort in extracting the scientific value from the transmitted word (al-kalimah al-manqulah).
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a summary of the Islamic method for verifying transmitted reports. The author begins by noting that Islamic scholarship developed specialized biographical dictionaries (qawamis li-dabt al-ashkhas wa al-rijal) that allow one to detect falsehood and weak interpolations with the same ease as correcting a word in a language dictionary. Furthermore, a distinct discipline called 'mustalah al-hadith' (hadith terminology) emerged, which integrates all the necessary components for investigating transmission and reports using a unique scientific methodology. The author presents this as a brief overview, encouraging those who seek deeper knowledge to study these arts, which he describes as containing an astonishing and miraculous effort in extracting scientific value from transmitted statements.

Key Terms

قواميس الرجال
النقل

Muslim scholars developed biographical dictionaries and hadith terminology as rigorous tools to verify the authenticity of transmitted reports.

Verifying Material Claims: The Necessity of Sensory Evidence
Buti establishes the methodological rule for verifying material claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's principle that verification methods vary by claim type and that material claims require empirical sensory evidence.

Core Idea
Material claims demand sensory evidence, and Islam embraces it.

Buti introduces a foundational methodological rule: how we verify a claim depends on what kind of claim it is. For claims about physical, material things, the only reliable path is through the five senses—what we now call experiment and observation. This passage sets the stage for a rational and empirical approach within Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the author's own phrasing establish the principle.
Notice the key terms: 'material existent' and 'five senses'.
2
Identify the classification of claims
Buti states that the verification path differs according to the type of claim. Focus on the category of material existents—what does he say about them?
The passage does not list all types, only material ones.
3
Reflect on the acceptance of empirical methods
Buti explicitly says Islam does not hesitate to adopt what is proven by sensory evidence. Consider how this aligns with modern science.
This counters the misconception that Islam is anti-empirical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السبيل المتخذة للتحقيق في الادعاء : يختلف هذا السبيل كما قلنا ، حسب اختلاف نوع الادعاء . فما كان منه متعلقاً بموجود مادي يتناوله تحليلاً أو تكييفاً ، فلا بد من الاعتماد فيه على شواهد وبراهين من الحواس الخمس ، أي على ما يسمى بالتعبير الحديث ( التجربة والمشاهدة ) . إذ هي الوسيلة الطبيعية إلى الإدراك اليقيني في مثل هذه الأمور. والإسلام لا يتردد في تبني كل ما يثبت تحقيقاً بهذه الوسيلة
The path taken for verification of a claim: This path differs, as we said, according to the difference in the type of claim. As for what pertains to a material existent, dealing with it by analysis or modification, then it is necessary to rely in it on evidences and proofs from the five senses, i.e., on what is called in modern expression (experiment and observation). For it is the natural means to certain perception in such matters. And Islam does not hesitate to adopt everything that is proven by this means.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a classification and methodological rule. The author states that the path for verifying a claim varies according to the type of claim. For claims related to material existents (mawjud madi), which involve analysis or modification, one must rely on empirical evidence: proofs from the five senses, which in modern terms are called experiment and observation (al-tajribah wa al-mushahadah). These are the natural means to attain certain knowledge in such matters. The author then affirms that Islam does not hesitate to accept whatever is proven through this method, showing compatibility between Islamic epistemology and empirical science.

Key Terms

موجود مادي (material existent)
الحواس الخمس (five senses)
التجربة والمشاهدة (experiment and observation)
اليقين (certainty)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Islam rejects empirical science or only relies on revelation for all knowledge.
Correction: Buti clarifies that for material claims, sensory evidence is necessary and Islam fully adopts proven empirical findings.

Key Takeaway
Islam affirms that sensory evidence is the proper method for verifying claims about material existence.

Islam and Science: Harmony and the Quran's Wisdom on Empirical Details
Buti explains the Quran's purposeful silence on scientific details and its harmony with science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran avoids detailing scientific laws and how this honors the intellect while maintaining harmony with science.

Core Idea
The Quran honors the intellect by leaving empirical discovery to human effort.

In this passage, Buti addresses a common question: How does Islam relate to modern science? He makes a striking claim—no scientific fact contradicts Islam. But more importantly, he explains the Quran's deliberate choice to remain silent on scientific details, revealing a profound respect for human reason and the scientific method.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Notice the flow: Buti first states the absence of contradiction, then explains why the Quran avoids scientific details, and finally distinguishes unseen reports.
Pay attention to the word 'secret' (السر) — he is unveiling the wisdom.
2
Identify the two key claims
Identify the two main ideas: (1) science does not contradict Islam, (2) the Quran intentionally does not detail empirical laws. Think about why these two points are connected.
3
Understand the reasoning for silence
Buti gives a reason: If the Quran detailed scientific laws, people would believe them by revelation rather than by experiment and observation. This would dishonor the intellect. Consider how this aligns with the Islamic emphasis on using reason.
The phrase 'out of honor for the intellect' (تكريماً للعقل) is central.
4
Contrast with unseen reports
Notice how Buti treats unseen (ghaybi) matters differently: the Quran details them because empirical methods cannot reach them. Certainty there comes only from revelation. This boundary is important.
Unseen reports include matters of the afterlife, angels, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما من الناحية العكسية ، فإن العلم لم يستطع أن يقدم لنا إلى اليوم أي حقيقة علمية تخالف أي جزئية من جزئيات العقيدة الإسلامية ولم يكلفنا شيء من الكتاب والسنة بأي معلومات خاصة صريحة تتعلق بالموجودات المادية القائمة من حولنا ، اللهم إلا ما أشار إليه منها في عبارات تحمل على الفكر والتأمل فيها أكثر من أن تبلغنا أي معلومات عنها ، وذلك اعتماداً على الوسائل والأسباب التي جهز الله بها الإنسان والتي هي الآلة الطبيعية لكشف لثام الجهل عن كل حقيقة مادية موجودة . وهذا هو السر في أن القرآن لم يفصل القول في القوانين العلمية المتعلقة بالمحسوسات والمشاهدات ، إذ إنه لو فعل ذلك لألزم الناس إذن ، بالإيمان بمقتضاها . فيكون ذلك حملاً للعقول على تبني حقائق علمية دون السلوك إليها في سبيل براهينها المنسجمة معها ، وهي التجربة والمشاهدة . وهذا مالا يحمل القرآن أحداً من الناس عليه ، تكريماً للعقل وإطلاقاً له ليسير في منهجه الطبيعي إلى کشف الحقائق المحسوسة ولذلك تجده في هذه القضايا لا يزيد على أن يدفع أرباب العقول إلى البحث بوسائلهم العلمية الكاشفة . أما مافيه من الإخبارات الغيبية فإنه قد فصل القول فيها بحكم مبرم ، لأنه لا مطمع عن طريق شيء من التجربة والمشاهدة في الوصول إليها . وليس السبيل إلى اليقين بها إلا خبر الله جل جلاله أو السنة المتواترة
As for the opposite side, science has not been able to present to us up to today any scientific fact that contradicts any detail of the Islamic creed. And nothing from the Book (Quran) or the Sunnah has imposed upon us any explicit specific information pertaining to the material existents around us, except what it pointed to in expressions that encourage thought and reflection in them more than conveying any information about them. That is relying on the means and causes that Allah has equipped man with, which are the natural instrument for lifting the veil of ignorance from every existing material reality. And this is the secret of why the Quran did not detail the scientific laws related to sensory and observable things. For if it had done so, it would then have obligated people to believe in them. That would be forcing minds to adopt scientific facts without traversing the path of their proofs that are consistent with them, namely experiment and observation. And this is something the Quran does not impose on anyone, out of honor for the intellect and freeing it to proceed in its natural method to discover sensory realities. Therefore you find it in these matters does not exceed urging the possessors of intellects to research using their scientific means of discovery. As for the unseen reports in it, it has detailed them with a decisive judgment, because there is no hope through anything of experiment and observation to reach them. And the path to certainty about them is only the report of Allah, may His majesty be exalted, or the mutawatir Sunnah.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an argument explaining the harmony between Islam and science, and the Quran's wisdom in not detailing empirical matters. The author first notes the absence of scientific facts contradicting any part of Islamic creed. He then observes that the Quran and Sunnah do not impose explicit scientific information about material things; any references to them are phrased to inspire thought and reflection rather than provide data. This is because Allah has endowed humans with natural means (the senses and reason) to discover material realities. The secret (al-sirr) behind the Quran's lack of detail on scientific laws is that if it had detailed them, it would obligate belief in them via revelation rather than through their proper proofs (experiment and observation), which would dishonor the intellect. Instead, the Quran honors the intellect by freeing it to investigate scientifically. Conversely, for unseen matters (akhbar ghaybiyyah), the Quran does provide detailed, decisive statements because empirical methods cannot reach them; certainty here comes only from Allah's report or the mutawatir Sunnah.

Key Terms
العقيدة الإسلامية (Islamic creed)
الكتاب والسنة (Book and Sunnah)
الآلة الطبيعية (natural instrument)
التجربة والمشاهدة (experiment and observation)
الإخبارات الغيبية (unseen reports)
السنة المتواترة (mutawatir Sunnah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran contains detailed scientific facts that were discovered later, proving its divine origin.
Correction: Buti argues the opposite: the Quran intentionally avoids such details to preserve the integrity of empirical science and honor human intellect. Its purpose is not to provide scientific textbooks but to guide spiritual and moral life.

Checkpoint

D) Because science and religion are separate domains

Key Takeaway
The Quran intentionally leaves empirical matters to human investigation to honor the intellect, while unseen matters require revealed certainty.

Certain Knowledge from Clear Texts in Quran and Mutawatir Sunnah
Buti classifies unseen claims and states the epistemological rule for certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how certain unseen claims (samiyyat) become certain knowledge through clear texts in the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah, grounded in the principle of tawatur.

Core Idea
Unseen claims with clear, mutawatir texts are certain knowledge.

Buti has just discussed sensory matters. Now he turns to unseen matters. He establishes a key epistemological rule: if an unseen claim has a clear text in the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah, it becomes certain knowledge because the Quran and mutawatir Sunnah are transmitted via tawatur, which guarantees certainty. This passage is foundational for understanding the source of certainty in Islamic theology regarding matters of the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Notice the distinction between sensory and unseen matters.
Pay attention to the term 'أمر تجريدي أو غيبي' (abstract or unseen matter).
2
Identify the two categories of unseen claims
The passage divides unseen claims into two categories: those with a clear text in the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah, and those without. Identify the phrase that marks this division.
Look for the phrase 'فمنه ما تجد... ومنه ما لا تجد'.
3
Understand the rule for certainty
Buti states that claims with a clear text are included in 'certain perceptions' (al-mudrakat al-yaqiniyyah). Grasp why: because their transmission goes back to the certain mutawatir report.
The path to certainty (sabil al-yaqin) is via tawatur.
4
Reflect on the grounding in tawatur
The Quran itself is transmitted via tawatur, so its words are definitely from Allah. Similarly, the mutawatir Sunnah is certain. This grounds the certainty of the texts.
Consider how this applies to claims about the afterlife and other unseen matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا فيما يتعلق بأمور محسوسة . وأما ماكان من الدعاوى متعلقاً بأمر تجريدي أو غيبي غير خاضع لشيء من الحواس الظاهرة ، فمنه ماتجد في الكتاب أو متواتر السنة نصاً واضحاً فيه ، ومنه ما لا تجد في شيء منها حديثاً واضحاً عنه . فأما المنصوص عليه في أحدهما : فهو داخـل بـذلـك في المدركات اليقينية . وسبيل اليقين به أنه من حيث نقل الكتاب أو السنة له ، يرجع إلى الخبر اليقيني المتواتر الذي فرغنا من البحث فيه . إذ القرآن إنما هو اللفظ الموحى به إلى صل عروسة والواصل إلينا عن طريق التواتر ، فلا جرم أن قرآنية ألفاظه مقطوع بها . ومثل القرآن في ذلك السنة إذا وصلت إلينا متواترة .
This concerns sensory matters. As for what pertains to an abstract or unseen matter not subject to any of the external senses, among them are those for which you find in the Book (Quran) or the mutawatir Sunnah a clear text, and among them are those for which you do not find in any of them a clear statement about it. As for what is stipulated in either of them, it is thereby included in certain perceptions. The path to certainty about it is that, in terms of the transmission of the Quran or Sunnah to him, it goes back to the certain mutawatir report which we have finished researching. For the Quran is only the wording revealed to [؟] (صل عروسة) and reaching us via tawatur, so inevitably the Quranicity of its words is definite. And like the Quran in that is the Sunnah if it reaches us as mutawatir.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a classification and epistemological rule regarding unseen claims. The author distinguishes between sensory matters (already discussed) and abstract/unseen matters (amr tajridi aw ghaybi) that are not subject to the senses. For such claims, some have a clear text in the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah, while others do not. Those with a clear text are thereby included in certain perceptions (al-mudrakat al-yaqiniyyah). The path to certainty (sabil al-yaqin) about them is that their transmission via the Quran or Sunnah traces back to the certain mutawatir report (al-khabr al-yaqini al-mutawatir), which the author says he has already researched. He then grounds this in the fact that the Quran is the wording revealed to the Prophet (صل عروسة – likely a corruption of صلى الله عليه وسلم) and transmitted to us through tawatur, so the Quranicity of its words is definite (maqtū‘ bihā). Similarly, the Sunnah is certain if it reaches us as mutawatir.

Key Terms
أمر تجريدي أو غيبي
نص واضح
المدركات اليقينية
الخبر اليقيني المتواتر
التواتر
قرآنية الألفاظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All claims about the unseen are certain because they come from Islamic sources.
Correction: Only those with clear, explicit texts in the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah are certain; other claims require different methods of verification.

Checkpoint

A) Its compatibility with reason
B) Its transmission via tawatur
C) The agreement of scholars
D) Personal spiritual experience

Key Takeaway
Unseen claims that have a clear text in the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah become certain knowledge because these sources are transmitted via tawatur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Qur'an's Restraint in Detailing Scientific Laws
Explains why the Qur'an does not detail scientific laws to preserve intellectual freedom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qur'an deliberately refrains from detailing empirical scientific laws, and how this honors human intellect.

Core Idea
The Qur'an leaves science to human reason and observation.

Why doesn't the Qur'an simply explain all scientific facts directly? In this passage, the author reveals the wisdom behind the Qur'an's restraint: it was never meant to be a science textbook. Instead, it equips humans with the tools of reason and observation, then invites them to discover the material world on their own. This approach honors the intellect and protects intellectual freedom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the key terms like 'وسائل وأسباب' (means and causes) and 'تكريماً للعقل' (honoring the intellect).
2
Identify the author's main argument
The author states a 'secret' (السر) behind why the Qur'an did not detail scientific laws. Find that statement and restate it in your own words.
Focus on the conditional 'if it had done so...'
3
Understand the consequence of detailing laws
Imagine if the Qur'an had given detailed scientific laws. What would that imply for believers? The passage says it would 'compel people to believe' without using their own reasoning.
This connects to the concept of intellectual freedom.
4
Reflect on the positive purpose
Instead, the Qur'an honors the intellect by leaving it free to use its natural method: experiment and observation. Ask yourself why this is a form of respect.
The phrase 'تكريماً للعقل' is key.
5
Apply the principle
Think of one example where the Qur'an prompts investigation without giving the answer (e.g., reflecting on creation). How does this match the author's explanation?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتماداً على الوسائل والأسباب التي جهز الله بها الإنسان والتي الآلة الطبيعية لكشف لثام الجهل عن كل حقيقة مادية موجودة • وهي وهذا هو السر في أن القرآن لم يفصل القول في القوانين العلمية المتعلقة بالمحسوسات والمشاهدات ، إذ إنه لو فعل ذلك لألزم الناس إذن ، بالإيمان بمقتضاها . فيكون ذلك حملاً للعقول على تبني حقائق علمية دون السلوك إليها في سبيل براهينها المنسجمة معها ، وهي التجربة والمشاهدة . وهذا مالا يحمل القرآن أحداً من الناس عليه ، تكريماً للعقل وإطلاقاً له ليسير في منهجه الطبيعي إلى کشف الحقائق المحسوسة ولذلك تجده في هذه القضايا لا يزيد على أن يدفع أرباب العقول إلى البحث بوسائلهم العلمية الكاشفة .
Relying on the means and causes with which God equipped man, which are the natural instrument for removing the veil of ignorance from every material existing reality. And this is the secret why the Qur'an did not detail the scientific laws related to sensibles and observables, for if it had done so, it would have compelled people then to believe in their implications. That would be a burdening of minds to adopt scientific truths without proceeding to them by way of their proofs consistent with them, namely experiment and observation. And this is something the Qur'an does not impose on anyone, honoring the intellect and freeing it to proceed in its natural method to discover sensible realities. Therefore, you find it in these matters does no more than prompt people of intellect to investigate by their own revelatory scientific means.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an argument explaining the Qur'an's methodology regarding empirical science. The author begins by stating that God equipped humans with means and causes—these are the natural instruments for uncovering material truths. He then reveals the secret (السر) behind why the Qur'an did not elaborate on scientific laws concerning observable phenomena: if it had done so, it would have forced people to accept those truths without using their own rational and empirical methods. That would contradict the honor (تكريماً) given to the intellect, which is meant to operate freely within its natural pathway. The Qur'an's role in these matters is merely to prompt thinkers to use their own scientific tools. The argument is that the Qur'an respects intellectual autonomy and avoids compelling belief in empirical matters.

Key Terms
الوسائل والأسباب (means and causes)
الآلة الطبيعية (natural instrument)
المحسوسات والمشاهدات (sensibles and observables)
التجربة والمشاهدة (experiment and observation)
تكريماً للعقل (honoring the intellect)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qur'an should be a comprehensive scientific textbook containing all empirical facts.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Qur'an deliberately avoids detailing scientific laws to preserve the intellect's freedom and to encourage humans to use their own God-given means of observation and experiment.

Checkpoint

A) Because they are not important for guidance

C) Because the Prophet was not a scientist
D) Because such laws are only for later generations

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an honors human intellect by not imposing scientific truths, instead encouraging investigation through reason and observation.

Two Stages of Verification for Qur'anic Certainty
Explains the two-stage verification process for Qur'anic certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-stage verification process that must be completed for Qur'anic texts to become a permanent source of certainty.

Core Idea
Certainty about Qur'anic content requires verifying both its transmission and its divine origin.

Shaykh Ramadan al-Bouti explains that knowing the Qur'an has been transmitted accurately is only half the journey. For absolute certainty about its content, we must also verify that the Prophet's claim to receive revelation is true. This passage outlines the two complementary stages that together establish the Qur'an as a source of certain knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to get the full meaning.
Pay attention to the distinction between transmission and content truthfulness.
2
Identify the two stages

The second stage depends on rules discussed later.
3
Understand the methodology
Note that the verification uses 'complete induction' (الاستقراء التام) and 'clear entailment' (اللزوم البين). Think about why these rational tools are necessary for the second stage.
These are rational proofs, not merely textual.

As for the truthfulness of what the Qur'an itself contains, regardless of it being a Qur'an reaching us from the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) with certainty, that is another scientific matter that enters into the second part of the claim related to abstract issues or unseen matters. Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of how certainty is obtained from Qur'anic content beyond mere transmission. The author distinguishes between the fact of the Qur'an's transmission (which gives certainty that these are the words of the Prophet) and the truthfulness of its content (that it is from God). He states that the latter requires a separate investigation into the phenomenon of revelation itself, based on certain proofs using complete induction (الاستقراء التام) and clear entailment (اللزوم البين). He then outlines two stages of consideration: first, verifying the chain of transmission (sanad) of the Qur'an from the Prophet to us; second, verifying that the Prophet's claim that the Qur'an is from God is true. Once the second stage is confirmed (using rules to be discussed later), the Qur'anic texts become a permanent source of certainty. He concludes that this is the meaning of his earlier statement that explicit texts enter into certain perceptions. The passage thus clarifies that scriptural certainty requires both external and internal verification.

Two Stages for Certainty from Quranic Texts
Buti outlines two stages for certainty from Quranic texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-stage methodology for obtaining certainty from Quranic definitive texts as outlined by Buti.

Core Idea
Certainty from the Quran requires two verifications: chain and divine source.

Buti here clarifies that the Quran's content does not automatically yield certainty. Instead, a rigorous process involving two distinct stages is necessary: first, verifying that the text has reached us reliably, and second, confirming that its message is indeed from Allah. This passage lays out the groundwork for this method, which will be elaborated later.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice Buti's careful phrasing about 'two stages'.
The passage contains a few unclear words due to OCR; focus on the clear logical structure.
2

Find where Buti enumerates the two stages. Stage one is about the chain of transmission (sanad). Stage two is about the Quran's claim of divine origin. Note that each stage builds on the other.
3

Buti mentions that the verification relies on 'complete induction' and 'clear implication'. Think about how these methods ensure certainty. They will be explained later.
This is a preview of upcoming concepts.
4
Reflect on why two stages are necessary
Consider why one stage is not enough. The first stage ensures the text is authentic; the second ensures its content is from Allah. Both must be satisfied for certainty.
Common mistake: thinking authenticity alone suffices.

Commentary

He concludes by linking this to an earlier statement: 'As for what is stipulated in one of them, it enters thereby into the certain perceptions.' The passage thus outlines a two-step methodology for establishing certainty from scriptural texts.
